Hishikari Suffers from Dysentery

(Changchun) Since the middle of last month, cholera and dysentery have been raging in the city, with Japanese patients being the most numerous. The South Manchuria Railway Hospital is extremely busy. Furthermore, according to an announcement made by the Kwantung Army at 2:00 PM today, Commander-in-Chief General Hishikari has been suffering from dysentery since yesterday morning. He developed a fever last night with a body temperature of 39 degrees, and has had severe diarrhea that has not stopped so far. His respiration is 90, and his pulse is 82. (9th Hualian dispatch)

Naval Negotiation Situation

(London) Colonel Iwashita, the naval expert dispatched by Japan to England for the naval preparatory talks, arrived here this afternoon. Iwashita's authority is not very extensive, and the talks to be conducted later will be purely consultative in nature. However, the British authorities, due to Japan's repeated development declarations over the past months and the inconsistencies therein, feel that they do not understand Japan's attitude and are eager to hear Iwashita's talks in order to understand Japan's intentions. Iwashita has two other tasks here: one is to hand over instructions from the Japanese government to the Japanese ambassador, and the other is to report on the recent technical reforms of the Japanese Navy to the Japanese naval attaché in the UK. (8th Havas dispatch)

(London) The Daily Telegraph reports that the naval talks recently conducted in London involved technical issues, and were not limited to procedural details. This level is now informally acknowledged by the general public. The most important technical issue discussed was the size of capital ship tonnage. The British government advocated limiting capital ships to 25,000 tons or 22,000 tons, and cruisers to 7,000 tons, but the American representatives firmly insisted on maintaining the current tonnage and did not support the British proposal. The disagreement between the two countries immediately became apparent. Although the British plan has been approved by Japan and France, there seems to be little hope of reaching a compromise based on this principle. Regarding the submarine issue, when French Naval Chief Pitorili came to England recently, he detailed France's views. Mr. Pitorili made it clear that France could not reduce its submarine strength. As for warships exceeding 1,850 tons, with gun calibers of 5 inches or 129 millimeters, which should be called cruisers, this is also difficult for France to accept. However, British experts believe that the French Navy has 31 leading ships with a maximum displacement of 3,000 tons and gun calibers of 5 and a half inches or 154 millimeters. According to the revision of the treaty, they should actually be treated as cruisers. Captain Picia, an Italian naval expert, also explained the reasons why his country decided to build 35,000-ton warships on the eve of the naval conference, and stated how his country's submarine and other light warship construction plans will be formulated, depending on the attitude of France. The Daily Telegraph also reported that these talks have caused a pessimistic impression among well-informed sources, because the opinions of various countries on fundamental issues of naval policy are very different, and this was revealed in these talks. (9th Havas dispatch)

High-Speed Aircraft

Twenty-Three Already in Production

Its combat power is comparable to that of reconnaissance aircraft. The Navy Department has 23 of these new aircraft under construction, and another 23 are being rebuilt. The Navy aircraft currently stationed in Hawaii, which recently flew non-stop from San Francisco to Honolulu, are also being upgraded. Their speed averages 130 miles per hour. This record-breaking aircraft, after further modification, will definitely lead the world in high-speed flight, and its direct flight capability is also unmatched by other aircraft. Hitler

Announces General Amnesty

Conspiracy to Rebel Not Included in Amnesty

President and Prime Minister's Powers Combined

Public Referendum Already Assured

(Berlin) President and Prime Minister Hitler has ordered a general amnesty for thousands of political prisoners in prisons and detention camps. This is a new initiative by Hitler after taking office as the head of Germany. Political prisoners who defamed Hitler personally or the government, or damaged the dignity of Germany, are all included in the amnesty. Radical elements of the National Socialist Party, except those who have committed riot, terrorist movement, or conspiracy to rebel, are not included in the scope of the amnesty. Stormtrooper leaders and secondary government officials who have been arrested or are under investigation due to the June 30th incident are regarded as the second category and are not eligible for the special benefits of the amnesty. Hitler has also ordered the investigation of criminals in detention camps, and declared that if the criminals can guarantee that they will no longer oppose the current government, they can be given a chance to rehabilitate themselves. The amnesty order also stipulates that the masterminds and others in the June 30th incident will be given a lenient investigation to allow for a lenient verdict. (9th National News Agency dispatch)

(Berlin) With the offices of German President and Prime Minister now held by Hitler alone, the German government has the opportunity to announce a general amnesty. A law will be issued tonight granting an amnesty. Not only will some political prisoners be pardoned, but this move by the Popular Will government almost says that the government is already assured of the result of the public vote on August 19th to approve the merger of the offices of President and Prime Minister. According to this law, anyone convicted of defaming Hitler can be pardoned. This amnesty applies to anyone sentenced to less than six months imprisonment and a fine of 1,000 marks, and to first-time offenders. However, crimes of treason, disclosure of military secrets, attempted assassination, and possession of weapons are not included in the amnesty. The regulations concerning the detention of suspects will be amended, secondary criminals can be spared, and the cases of those arrested for the Rohm affair will also be re-examined. (9th Reuters dispatch)

(Berlin) Germany is scheduled to hold a public referendum on August 19th to vote on the law that allows Hitler to hold the powers of both President and Prime Minister. The propaganda campaign is about to begin, and Propaganda Minister Goebbels is scheduled to broadcast a speech on August 13th, before the end of the national mourning period on August 16th. Hitler is scheduled to speak to the public on August 17th. (9th Havas dispatch)

Current Commentary

On the Yuguan British Troop Exercise Incident

The Yuguan British troop exercise incident has attracted attention for more than ten days. British and Japanese soldiers faced each other during the exercise, as if in a state of war. There was once a rumor that a British soldier was injured by a stray bullet from the Japanese side, and the situation was serious. However, it was later reported that the British troop exercise had ended. Both the British and Japanese sides claimed that the rumor of a British soldier being injured was untrue and denied it.

We believe that even if a British soldier was accidentally injured, it is a trivial issue and has nothing to do with the overall situation. Even at the current stage, the diplomatic relations between the two countries will not be broken due to this local exercise incident. What is incomprehensible is that a mere few hundred British soldiers are conducting routine exercises under the serious vigilance of the Japanese side. It is obvious that it is not enough to endanger the existence of Manchukuo. The Kwantung Army's advocacy of opposition is unnecessarily making a mountain out of a molehill. If it is said that the Kwantung Army is doing so out of resentment for the policy of non-recognition by various countries and is deliberately making things difficult, then its impact will only increase unnecessary antipathy. What good will it do for Manchukuo? Moreover, after the September 18th Incident, countries such as Britain and France still enjoy extraterritoriality rights in Manchuria. The Japanese themselves still occupy the Liaodong Peninsula and the South Manchuria Railway zone. All these facts are based on and justified by Chinese-foreign treaties. Now, the British troop exercise and the repeated actions of the Japanese troops in the Pingjin area are based on the Boxer Protocol. If a Kwantung Army that does not bear the mission of international diplomacy must insist on its prejudice, saying that certain treaties between China and foreign countries (including Japan) can be applied to Manchukuo, while others cannot, then it is certain that the countries concerned will not remain silent, and will also put their own governments in what position. Now, let us take a step back and assume that the Kwantung Army generally has the power to speak for Manchukuo in terms of law and fact. Then, it is tantamount to admitting that Manchukuo is not an independent country. Since Manchukuo is not an independent country, and the Japanese do not recognize it as a vassal state, then it goes without saying that it is not entitled to have a fixed border. If the Kwantung Army knows that Manchukuo is not entitled to have a fixed border, and yet deliberately creates disputes over the Sino-"Manchu" border, then how will it justify itself?

Moreover, we would also like to add a word. The British military general this time said that the area outside the Great Wall is Chinese territory, and notified our Shanhaiguan Special Public Security Bureau of the exercise location and subjects. The propriety of his handling is obvious to the world. However, the Boxer Protocol allows various countries to station troops in several designated locations to protect the "capital" to the sea passage, so as to avoid any interruption. The main purpose is to guarantee the security of the embassy area in Dongjiaominxiang to avoid a repeat of the Boxer Rebellion. Now that the Chinese people have absolutely no intention or fact of blindly rejecting foreigners, and the capital has moved south to Nanjing on the Yangtze River with water and land transportation, the so-called embassy area in Dongjiaominxiang has no meaning to continue to exist. Various countries, in view of international practice and friendship with China, have the need to withdraw their troops as soon as possible. It is not possible to use unequal treaties as a talisman. Moreover, China has been bound by unequal treaties for more than eighty years. Although we are heartbroken by these countless shackles, our pursuit of liberation has always been carried out with open and aboveboard means. Before the treaty obligations are lifted, we have always faithfully fulfilled them without any change. What we expect from our friendly nations is only that they faithfully fulfill the treaty obligations related to us. However, since the September 18th Incident, the contracting parties of the so-called League of Nations Covenant, the Nine-Power Treaty, and the Kellogg-Briand Pact have all evaded each other, abandoning their obligations. As a result, the pain of unequal treaties is borne by us alone, and the benefits of equal treaties are not shared with us. When implementing unequal treaties, they are afraid of China's demise. When fulfilling equal treaties, they despise China's existence. The true face of international treaties has come to this. Do those of our friendly nations who enjoy the rights of unequal treaties have any feelings in their hearts?

Speech by the Associated Press Far East Manager

Mostly War in the Far East

Results of Japan's Military and Economic Aggression

Former Associated Press Far East Manager, Mr. Von Meier, gave a speech today at the annual Current Affairs Conference, stating that the Far East situation contains many elements of war, and the tendency towards peace is gradually disappearing. Mr. Von Meier said that the future of the Far East depends entirely on the development of the following four recent situations: (1) Japan's unilateral creation of "Manchukuo"; (2) Anglo-Japanese trade war; (3) Philippine independence and its consequences; (4) Washington Naval Treaty.

The most important of these is the "Manchukuo" problem, which indicates Japan's determination to expand its power in northern Asia. Japanese people generally claim that this expansion is not territorial aggression, but they cannot deny that it is economic aggression. Moreover, they cannot deny that every time Japanese economic power develops in northern Asia, it invariably uses force to maintain its gains. Taking Manchuria as an example, the Japanese still claim that the use of force is to compel the Chinese and Manchurian authorities to complete their newly established economic agreements. The Japanese believe that China has violated these agreements and deprived the Japanese of their rights. However, the reason why China is unwilling to recognize them is that these agreements were obtained by force. Therefore, Japan disregards everything and still uses force to remove the so-called "treacherous" Chinese authorities and replace them with the so-called "trustworthy" "Manchukuo." In order to ensure that "Manchukuo" is trustworthy, Japan is doing its best to ensure that the Japanese control all its military, political, and economic powers. This Japanese plan has been very successful in Manchuria, but whether it can be effective elsewhere is another question. Researchers of the Far East issue believe that Japan will replicate this model near Siberia, Vladivostok, and Kamchatka, because Japan's position there is similar to that in Manchuria. Japan also has agreements with Soviet Russia, which allow the Japanese to fish in Soviet territorial waters. The Japanese have repeatedly claimed that Soviet Russia is untrustworthy, so if there is an opportunity, Japan may also create a country similar to Manchukuo in the Siberian coastal province. Japanese authorities absolutely deny this, saying that Japan's economic relations in Siberia are far less significant than in Manchuria, and the Russo-Japanese agreements are not as important as the Sino-Japanese agreements regarding Manchuria. Furthermore, the historical background is very different. The Russo-Japanese War broke out because of the Manchurian problem. Although Japan also sent troops to Siberia in 1918, it was incomparable to the Russo-Japanese War. Some people believe that it seems more likely that Japan will implement this plan in Mongolia, because the border between Manchuria and Mongolia is complex, and Japan has repeatedly tried to get Mongolian princes to support the organization of "Manchukuo." Many agreements have now been established, and disputes may arise in the future. The Japanese side also dismisses this as pure speculation, saying that the boundaries of Manchuria will naturally be clarified in the future, and the relations between Inner and Outer Mongolia and Soviet Russia will also be resolved. As it stands, Russia and Japan will definitely not go to war over Mongolia, and Russia can emulate Japan in Mongolia before Japan takes action, creating a country friendly to Russia, and Japan will be helpless.

The Anglo-Japanese trade war is the result of the European War and the Washington Conference. The European War made Japan a first-class industrial and commercial power, and the Washington Conference dissolved the Anglo-Japanese alliance. As a result, the two countries have become fierce competitors in Asian and world markets. Japan benefited greatly from the European War because countries had no time to engage in industry and commerce. It took the opportunity to revitalize factories and expand shipping. Therefore, although Britain had long occupied the Asian cotton textile market, it could not compete with Japan in this regard. Even in Manchester, the base of British cotton textiles, the price of Japanese products was lower than that of British goods. The area where Britain suffered the most losses was India. In 1931, Japanese goods almost occupied the Indian market, leaving no room for British goods. Britain then announced the abolition of the Indo-Japanese trade agreement, and Japan agreed to limit exports to India. After several negotiations, a compromise was reached. Japan claims that Britain is sparing no effort to create difficulties for Japanese goods. Even the League of Nations' refusal to recognize "Manchukuo" and China's anti-Japanese movement are all instigated by Britain behind the scenes. Therefore, the current situation between Britain and Japan in the Far East is quite volatile.

The results of the Philippine issue after the United States approved independence are quite important. China is now in a state of panic because the islands in the Pacific Ocean under Japanese mandate have largely surrounded China's gateway. If the Philippines are added, there will be no way out. After the United States withdraws from the Philippines, Japan will inevitably occupy it, which has become inevitable in the minds of the Chinese. The economic power of the Japanese in the Philippines is already considerable. If political control is added in the future, it will become a second "Manchukuo." This statement is based on the dissatisfaction of the Chinese with Japan, but the Japanese side also feels a kind of uneasiness. They believe that after the Philippines becomes independent, it will change the current situation in Asia, and Japan has not yet resolved the northern issue, so it has no time to take care of it. If other countries engage in any political activities in the Philippines, how can Japan sit idly by? Moreover, Britain and the Netherlands also feel that this tendency toward independence has a risk of spreading because their territories are close to the Philippines, so it is difficult to predict the future situation. As for the results of the Washington Conference, it is still not possible to fully assess them. Japan is planning to abolish the existing naval ratio, and as for the Nine-Power Treaty guaranteeing China's territorial integrity, the Chinese side believes that it has long been torn up by Japan. Japan absolutely denies this, and other countries have not given up on it, but the so-called treaty is actually equivalent to waste paper. At this time of global turmoil, with increasingly fierce economic competition, the weak countries of Asia are in danger of being crushed like eggs. (National Telegram, 8th)

U.S. Nationalizes Silver

Specifies 50.01 Cents per Ounce in U.S. Dollars

New York Silver Market Futures Trading Halted as a Result

Silver Imports Valued Over $100 Require Consular Certificate

(Washington) President Roosevelt announced the nationalization of silver. (Reuters Urgent Dispatch, 9th)

(Washington) An executive order stipulates that in accordance with the Silver Purchase Act of 1934, silver is to be nationalized at a price of 50.01 cents per ounce. Silver market futures trading was halted immediately due to this order. (Reuters Dispatch, 9th)

(Washington) U.S. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau issued an order today stating that all silver imported into the United States, with a value of more than $100, must have a consular certificate. The order is similar to the recently promulgated regulations managing gold. However, silver bars in transit and silver goods that are imported and then re-exported are not subject to this restriction. The Treasury Secretary stated that the purpose of issuing the order is to collect statistics on silver imports into the United States. (National Telegram, 8th)

(London) Since August 1st, the price of silver has risen sharply by one penny. All sectors here are now paying attention to this matter, and are discussing the impact of the rise in silver prices on the purchasing power of the East, and the future trend of silver prices. People in the silver camp all say that the United States is still the pivot of the overall situation. The U.S. government has recently been buying silver in large quantities here and in New York at gradually increasing prices, so India has also slightly increased its purchases, while China has sold it. However, it is now heard that the supply in London is already limited. If the U.S. authorities continue to purchase, the market price will continue to rise. However, experts advise caution, saying that once the United States stops buying, the price of silver will plummet. Even if New York speculators purchase Indian silver reserves, many positions remain open, and it cannot be guaranteed that the market price will not fall when the United States stops buying. (Reuters Dispatch, 9th)

U.S. Drought Affects Cotton Harvest

Decrease of 25% Compared to Last Year

Production Control Not Necessarily Production Restriction

Bankhead Act Clauses Must Still Be Implemented Next Year

(Washington) The Department of Agriculture announced that this year's cotton harvest is expected to reach 9,195,000 bales, a decrease of 3,852,000 bales compared to last year, a decrease of 25%. This is also a decrease of 5,480,000 bales compared to the average from 1928 to 1932. It is the lowest amount since 1921, when the cotton harvest was below 8 million bales. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

(Washington) Undersecretary of Agriculture, Mr. Wallace, stated today that American cotton may disappear from the world market in 1935. The difficulty facing American cotton production is whether to continue producing enough cotton so that the country can export 8 million bales of cotton as in the past, or to withdraw from the world cotton market altogether and only produce enough for domestic use. Normally, world consumption of American cotton is 14.8 million bales, of which 8 million bales are never exported. If farmers are willing to maintain their position in the 1935 world market, the government has the necessity of canceling production restrictions. After the Food Report Committee announced the cotton statistics for August this morning, Wallace immediately held a lengthy meeting with officials from the Department of Agriculture. The above statement was released after the meeting. The published figures, only 9,195,000 bales of cotton, were far from what the Department of Agriculture had initially expected, so Wallace immediately convened senior officials from the Department of Agriculture to discuss the matter after the number was announced. Wallace's attitude is that the cotton issue should be handled by the farmers themselves. The cotton production in 1934 was beyond expectations. If requested by the planters, the government may cancel the mandatory restrictions of the Bankhead Act. The decision of the Department of Agriculture was greatly unexpected, because the Department of Agriculture stated after the meeting that it would be a great mistake not to maintain 10 million bales of cotton within the limits of the Bankhead Act. It is rumored that the Agricultural Adjustment Administration is deeply afraid of causing resentment among the producers if it does not express anything, because the cotton producers voluntarily restrict cotton production because they expect the benefits after restricting production. However, officials from the Department of Agriculture sometimes solemnly stated that production control is not necessarily production restriction. Mr. Isakil, Wallace's economic advisor, told the American Cooperative Society that our goal must ultimately focus on more production to supply a richer life in everyone's desires. Some responsible parties insist on increasing cotton production in 1935, so that the production amount is priced between 12,500,000 bales and 13,000,000 bales. (National Telegram, 8th)

Heatwave Ravages the United States

Temperature as High as 115 Degrees

Breaks 62-Year Record

Crop and Livestock Damage Extremely Heavy

Grain Prices Soar in Chicago

(New York) The heatwave continues to prevail in the central part of China [obviously a typo for United States]; the temperature in Wharton, Washington, is as high as 115 degrees Fahrenheit, the highest record in 62 years. (Havas Dispatch, 9th)

(New York) Since the United States was invaded by the heatwave, the total number of deaths has reached 1,500. Now, a new heatwave is attacking, originating from the Rocky Mountains and the Appalachian Mountains, and extending to the southern parts of the Gulf of Mexico, so the number of deaths is increasing rapidly. Severe gales are raging in several places, and crops and livestock have suffered a lot of damage, so the disaster is becoming more serious. Chicago authorities have already slaughtered about a million heads of cattle, and are now purchasing another 850,000 heads to be slaughtered. It is believed that another 5 million heads of cattle will have to be sacrificed in the future. Currently, several cities are extremely hot. The temperature in Wharton, Washington, reached 114 degrees, Kansas City and Missouri both reached 108 degrees, and Springfield reached 105 degrees. The Washington Rural Loan Office has now designated Oklahoma as an emergency relief area, and can request food loans. The bureau currently has lending locations in 21 states, totaling 993 counties. Grain prices in Chicago soared today, creating a new record, because speculators, after receiving news of poor harvests, rushed to buy. (Reuters Dispatch, 8th)

Mourning Dollfuss

Austrian Leader Addresses 300,000 People

Uphold Independence, Guarantee Peace

Murder Act Borders on Banditry

Irreconcilable with National Socialism

Today's gathering was organized to commemorate Dr. Dollfuss. Many government officials also attended. When Prime Minister Schuschnigg gave his speech, he said that the government cannot reconcile with those who murdered Dr. Dollfuss, but only wishes to shake hands with all patriotic workers. (Reuters Dispatch, 8th)

A grand ceremony was held today in Vienna's "King Square" to commemorate the late Prime Minister Dollfuss. No less than 100,000 people participated. Prime Minister Schuschnigg denounced the crimes of the insurgents, praised Dollfuss's achievements, and urged the Austrian people to unite to support the independent and free Austria, as a guarantee of European culture and peace. Papen's Mission to Austria

Claims to Be Carrying Out the Late President's Wishes

Seeking to Restore Normal Relations Between the Two Countries

(Berlin) German Ambassador to Austria, Mr. von Papen, told a Reuters reporter today that I have received this mission in order to fulfill it in its meaning and spirit, because I know that the relaxation of tension in Europe depends on the realization of this mission, and I can use this to serve the country. Papen then said that the Prime Minister sent him a letter on July 26, explaining the work he should do as ambassador to Austria. Papen then quoted the words in the last letter sent to him by the late President Hindenburg, who signed the letter, saying that the reason for appointing him as the German diplomatic representative to Vienna was "because I hope that you can restore the good relations that our people have with the Austrian people on a daily basis. They are of the same race as us. I wish you success in carrying out this responsible work." Papen also said that this order is also a will at the same time, and there is no need to add anything to it. Papen ended his speech with the words "Hail Hitler." Heavy Rain Causes Disaster in Tongxu

(Kaifeng) The magistrate of Tongxu County telegraphed the Provincial Relief Association on the 9th, saying that due to continuous heavy rain, the entire county has become a swamp. Boats can reach the borders of Taikang and Fugou directly. The autumn crops have all been submerged and died. (Special Dispatch, 9th)

Tax on Foreign Rice to Relieve Rural Areas

Still Needs Overall Planning

(Nanjing) Chairman Yu Xuezhong of Hebei Province and others previously submitted a request to the Executive Yuan, asking that all tax revenue from foreign rice be allocated as a special fund to relieve rural areas in various provinces. The Executive Yuan meeting handed it over to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry to discuss and reply. The two ministries have sent representatives to discuss it once. As a result, it was decided that this matter relates to national tax revenue and needs overall planning before a decision can be made. It is currently considered that further research is necessary. (Special Dispatch, 9th)

(Nanjing) Rural Reconstruction Association member Gu Xinyi sent a letter to attend the grain control conference. According to him, the outflow of rice and grain from Shanghai has been very strong recently. The reason is that Nanjing, Jiangxi, Zhejiang, and other places are concentrated in Shanghai for procurement. Taking Jiangxi Province as an example, this time there are as many as one million dan [a unit of dry measure] purchased in Shanghai, which has caused the rice price in Shanghai to rise daily. Foreign rice imports have recently reached 3 million dan. At the current time of demand from all parties, injecting this quantity can also suppress rice prices a lot. Otherwise, it would have already soared to the highest peak. However, foreign rice imports must be limited, otherwise it may affect the entire rural economy in the future. The government authorities should pay attention to it. Gu also said that the foreign rice import tax should be changed by the government at any time. If there is a need for foreign rice, the tax rate should be reduced. When the price of foreign rice is extremely high, imports should be prohibited, and the import tax should be collected according to regulations. The current fixed method should be reconsidered: (1) When the price of foreign rice rises to 6-7 yuan, the import tax should be completely exempted to prevent the selling price from increasing due to taxation. (2) When the price of foreign rice rises to 9 yuan, the tax should be halved to slightly restrict it. (3) If it continues to rise to more than 10 yuan, the full tax should be collected or even the original tax rate should be increased to prevent large-scale imports. This method will be presented to the Central Government by the Shanghai Municipal Government and the authorities of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces for adoption. (Special Dispatch, 9th)

(Nanjing) The Examination Yuan held a meeting on the 9th to discuss the following important cases: (1) The Peiping Graduates' Professional Sports Federation requested the recruitment of graduate students and the reform of the examination system. It drafted a proposal to be submitted to the Examination Committee. It was decided to hand it over to Huang Xuyuan to draft a method, and then submit it to the meeting for discussion. (2) Investigate the names and numbers of graduates each year as a standard for recruitment. Decision: Discuss the detailed method and consult with the Ministry of Education to formulate it. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 9th)

The 6th Division of the puppet 3rd Army and the 61st and 63rd Regiments stubbornly resisted by taking advantage of the terrain. Our infantry and artillery bombarded the bandits fiercely, and the planes concentrated their firepower to bomb them fiercely. A total of four hundred and several bandits were killed, and dozens of guns were seized. The remnants of the bandits retreated to Xiacun Gaoshan and are still being pursued. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

Upper Reaches of the Yellow River Rising Rapidly

(Kaifeng) The upper reaches of the Yellow River are rising rapidly. The Yellow River Conservancy Commission received a telegram from the Tongguan Hydrological Station, stating that the river water rose sharply by half a meter early on the 8th. At 5:00, the water level reached 392.05 meters, and the flow rate was 3,800 cubic meters per second. In addition, the Shaanzhou Hydrological Station telegraphed that the water level at noon on the 8th was 292.66 meters, and the flow rate was 3,100 cubic meters per second, an increase of about one meter compared to noon on the 7th. Furthermore, according to a telegram from Dali, Shaanxi, the Luo River rose sharply by 1,500 cubic meters per second on the 8th. In addition, according to a telegram from Sanyuan, Shaanxi, the water level of the Jing River reached 440.80 meters at 6:00 on the 8th, and the flow rate was 500 cubic meters per second, an increase of about two and a half meters compared to the 6th. The Commission considered that the water level in the upper reaches had reached a dangerous level, and urgently telegraphed the situations of the steep rises in each river to the river affairs bureaus of the three provinces, instructing them to take precautions. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 9th)

(Kaifeng) The Yellow River at Tongguan rose by half a meter on the 8th, and Shaanzhou rose by one meter. (Special Dispatch, 9th)

Wolves Devour People in Northern Huangpi

(Hankou) Rice prices in various counties have risen to eight or nine yuan per dan. The price increase in Hankou is particularly severe, with a rise of over three yuan per dan in a few days. International Commercial Telegrams

|August 9th Reuters Special Business Report|

Gold and Silver

London gold price: The gold price today (9th) is 138 shillings and 1 pence, half a pence higher than yesterday.

London silver bar: The main reason for today's (9th) rise in silver prices is purchases by the United States, but Chinese bankers are selling and supply is not large. The market is uncertain. The spot price is 21 pence and 4375, up half a pence. Futures are also 21 pence and 4375, up 4375.

The New York silver bar market opened down 30 points, but later recovered about 40 points. The far-term silver market opened down 20 to 30 points compared to yesterday's closing price.

Exchange Rates

British-American: This morning (9th) in the London foreign exchange market, the US dollar improved compared to the previous day due to short covering in Europe. The opening exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar was unchanged at 5 yuan and 05.375 points. At 11:00 AM, it fell by 4375 points. At 12:00 PM, it fell by another 125 points. At 1:00 PM, it fell by another 125 points to 5 yuan and 04.6875 points. This price remained unchanged at 2:00 PM. Also, one US dollar is equivalent to 3 shillings, 11 pence, and 555 of British gold.

British-French: The opening price was 76 francs and 34, the same as yesterday's price. At 11:00 AM, it fell by 3 points to 76 francs and 32, but at 1:00 PM, it recovered 2 points to 76 francs and 34. Until 2:00 PM, there was no change.

American-British: This morning in the New York foreign exchange market, the British pound fell slightly. The opening exchange rate between the US dollar and the British pound was 5 yuan and 04.875 points, down half a point. Later, it rose to 5 yuan and 05 points. This price remained unchanged before noon.

Securities

Before the opening of the New York Stock Exchange, the factors favorable to the market were: (1) the commodity market continues to be strong; (2) the general opinion is that pessimism has recently subsided, and the market has an oversold appearance. The unfavorable factors for the market were: (1) industrial news is currently not exciting; (2) the export volume for July is estimated to decrease to about 485,000 tons, while the export volume for June was 985,000 tons. When the securities market opened this morning, sentiment was stable, with minimal fluctuations. Trading remains cautious. Merchants are waiting for the clarification of the commercial outlook, so there are no major fluctuations in securities.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The cotton market opened slightly lower today (9th) because many parties were closing positions. However, this was offset by purchases from the industry, and prices gradually trended upward. The recent price for October futures is up 5 points compared to the opening.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was firm today. At 1:00 PM, the price for October futures was 7.19, up 5 points.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market opened strong today due to favorable external news. At 1:00 PM, the price for October futures was 6 shillings, 3 pence, and 875, up 875 compared to yesterday's closing price.

American Wheat: The wheat market opened with a slight increase and continued to rise. The general opinion is that prices will rise further.

Rubber

New York Rubber: Rubber opened slightly lower but recovered to yesterday's closing price.

Page 11

Current Situation of the Puppet Organization Under Japanese Rule

All Manchukuo Puppet Troops Commanded by Japanese Officers

State Councilors Hold All Real Power in Political Affairs

Japanese Implements Ethnic Eradication Education in the Northeast

Special dispatch from Beiping: A visitor who came to Beiping from the Northeast described the recent situation in the Northeast, which is recorded in detail below:

Governance Situation

After the puppet Puyi claimed to be the "Emperor," the military and political affairs of the puppet organization have been completely controlled by the Japanese.

(A) Regarding military affairs, the puppet military department is the highest military organ. In addition to commanding all "Manchukuo" puppet troops, it also governs the Xiangwei Army Corps Headquarters, the Navy River Defense Fleet Command, the Central Military Training Office, the Horse Administration Bureau, the Jing'an Army, etc. The "Man" troops throughout the territory of the puppet organization are under the constant surveillance of the Japanese army, and most of the officers are Japanese, who exercise full command authority, so that there is no freedom of movement. The military strength is estimated at 26 mixed brigades, each brigade has two regiments, and each regiment has three battalions. Those stationed in Jilin have two battalions per regiment, totaling about 100,000 people. The Japanese army stationed in the Northeast has one division in Fengtian, one division and two gendarmerie regiments in Jilin (the puppet capital), two divisions in Heilongjiang and northern Manchuria, and one division in Rehe, totaling more than 100,000 people. Moreover, the number of Japanese veterans and immigrants in Dongbian County is no less than 200,000. Their goal is probably against Russia. All new-style firearms used by the puppet army have been confiscated by the Japanese, and there are no machine guns or artillery. The scale of the Fengtian Arsenal is the largest in China, and it is now operating according to Japanese plans. The navy has only recently built two 50-ton gunboats and four 14-ton gunboats in the River Defense Fleet, which can be completed soon. As for all technical construction projects in the puppet state, such as military surveys and military maps, they are all specified in the Japan-Manchukuo Agreement and are the responsibility of Japan.

(B) In terms of political affairs, the organization of various ministries and departments of the puppet state is the same as during Puyi's tenure as puppet executive, except that the title of director-general has been changed to minister. The anomalies are: (1) The Japanese, in the name of state councilors, control the overall political affairs of the puppet state. The current state councilor, Usa Katsuo, occupies the position of Zheng Xiaoxu, the prime minister of the puppet state. His seal cannot endorse the political affairs of the state without Usa's agreement. (2) The establishment of a general affairs department in each agency to control all administrative affairs of the puppet state. (3) The establishment of councilors in local administrative agencies to control local administration. All county administrations in the Northeast are measures implemented by the councilors.

Social Conditions

(A) Transportation: Since occupying the four northeastern provinces, Japan has worked hard to manage transportation. Last year, an agreement was concluded between the puppet state and the South Manchuria Railway to operate the existing railways under entrustment. The entire territory's Fengshan, Shenhai, Jichang, Jihai, Jihui, Jidun, Taoang, Qike, Taosuo, and Huhai nine lines have all been handed over to Japan. In addition, the South Manchuria Railway is rushing to build the Duntu line between Dunhua and Tumen, the Haike line between Keshan and Hailun, and the Labin line between Lafa and Harbin. Other harbors, waterway transportation, and all related businesses are also operated by the Japanese.

(B) Education: There are 11,395 elementary schools, 190 middle schools, 67 vocational schools, and 123 normal schools in the four northeastern provinces. Recently, there have been more additions. They are now full of Japanese teachers, and many are Japanese principals. The curriculum focuses on Japanese language, and it is also mixed with the so-called Wangdao (Kingly Way) ideology and the glorious history of Japan, etc., in order to erase the national character of our 30 million compatriots.

(C) Rural Conditions: Nineteen out of ten people in the Northeast are immigrants from Hebei and Shandong provinces, so farmers are the backbone of the people in the Northeast. After the September 18th Incident, farmers could not bear the oppression and trampling of the Japanese police and plainclothes detectives. At the same time, due to the armed immigration of Japanese and Koreans, they had to migrate to avoid them.

(D) Commercial Conditions: The Northeast has already become a market exclusively for Japan. Japanese goods are everywhere. Occasionally, there are Western goods or Russian goods such as calico, kerosene, etc., but due to heavy taxes and high prices, they cannot compete with Japanese goods. As for domestic goods, in addition to native cloth, Jilin ginseng, pork, lamb, and beef, chickens and ducks are also mostly transported from Russia. Fruits such as watermelons, peaches, apricots, apples, pears, etc., are transported from Dalian and Taiwan. Factories in various places are generally controlled by the Japanese. The large Chinese businesses in the Northeast have closed down one after another, so the once prosperous ports are gradually becoming desolate. Only opium dens, brothels, and small restaurants are still thriving. Apart from these three, there is no commercial activity to speak of. (7th)

Flooding on the Beiping-Suiyuan Railway

Repairs Completed at Damaged Sections

丨Full Traffic Resumed on the 3rd丨

Ping Report: This year, Sui Province has experienced many days of excessive rain, causing significant flooding, unprecedented in the last twenty years. The Ping-Sui Railway suffered particularly heavy damage. Partial disruption to traffic began on July 6th, and after heavy rains on the 13th, the damage became severe. After active repairs, all sections except for a landslide at Sandaoying, which still required extensive work, were fully repaired and traffic resumed on the 23rd. Unexpectedly, on the 25th, another heavy rain occurred, causing further damage to the newly repaired sections, even more extensive than before. Through continuous day and night repairs by the construction teams, and despite repeated heavy rains during the work period, full traffic was finally restored on the 3rd of this month. A summary of the key repairs on each section is provided below. As for a fundamental solution, it is said that the route will need to be changed, as the current route runs alongside the river, or even built directly within the riverbed. Therefore, it is impossible to prevent damage during major floods. The line has been damaged twice before, in the 13th and 18th years of the Republic. If the line is not changed, future troubles are inevitable. (1) Between Pingdiquan and Sanchakou: near Road House No. 168, west of Pingdiquan Station, the roadbed was adjacent to the Ba Wang River. This time, the river changed its course, washing away the original earth dam and directly hitting the roadbed, causing three breaks. Three temporary roads have now been repaired, and traffic resumed on the 17th. (2) Between Zhuozishan and Fushengzhuang: near the distant signal west of Zhuozishan Station, the stone dam at the north end of Bridge No. 493 was washed away. The roadbed west of the bridge was completely destroyed, for a length of approximately two li. Repairs were completed on the 23rd. (3) Between Fushengzhuang and Sandaoying: A. Bridge No. 501, west of Fushengzhuang, has been prone to silting or sand covering the tracks during rains over the years, preventing traffic. This year, the downstream route had been changed, and a new bridge was being built, along with a stone dam upstream. However, before the project was completed, heavy rains washed away the new dam and damaged the earthworks on the new line. The dam was then rebuilt using reinforced concrete to ensure its strength, and the earthworks on the new line were repaired. Water now flows smoothly through the new bridge without posing a risk of collapse. B. Bridge No. 509, west of Fushengzhuang, previously had insufficient openings. This year, two 12-foot culverts were added to the west side of the original bridge. Before the bridge work was completed, the riverbed had not yet been constructed when heavy floodwaters scoured out the riverbed, causing the bridge abutments and piers to collapse. The new earthworks at both ends were also washed away. In order to resume traffic quickly, the bridge openings were temporarily filled in. If there are no major floods, it should be safe. C. From Road House No. 197 eastward at Sandaoying, the route runs along the mountain. During this flood, the hillside collapsed for a length of 1100 feet, overlooking a deep river. It was impossible to bypass the route, so the mountainside had to be cut away to allow traffic to pass. Work began on July 20th, and efforts were made day and night to complete the repairs and resume traffic on the 31st. (The deepest cut into the mountain was 26 feet). (4) Between Sandaoying and Qixiaying: A. A total of five sections of roadbed were washed away between the two stations. The fourth section, near Road House No. 201, was the most dangerous. The first three sections were quickly repaired with temporary roads after the first major flood. The fourth section, after a large temporary road was constructed, was further damaged. The temporary road was then moved further away from the river, bypassing the back of Road House No. 201 to avoid the water. B. 1600 feet of roadbed were washed away west of Bridge No. 529, east of Qixiaying. The original wooden pile bridge with two openings and Bridge No. 530 were also destroyed. The upstream stone dam was breached, and the rushing water made repairs extremely difficult. A new earthen dam was built upstream to stop the flow of water, and a reinforced concrete dam was quickly built at the site of the original stone dam, while the roadbed was being filled in. Fortunately, the weather cleared up, and work was completed and traffic resumed on the 3rd of this month. (5) Between Qixiaying and Taobqi: The roadbed west of Erdahe Shantong, which originally ran along the mountain, was washed away for a length of about 700 feet. Overlooking a deep river, there was no place to obtain soil for filling. Mountain cutting was combined with temporary road repairs, and the repairs were completed and traffic resumed on July 23rd. (7th)

German Envoy in Peiping Commemorates

President Hindenburg

More Than 400 Chinese and Western Officials and Guests Attend

Venue Set at Xiehe Church, Ceremony Solemn

Peiping Communication: German Minister Trautmann convened German expatriates at Xiehe Church today (the 7th) to hold a memorial service for President Hindenburg, and invited Chinese officials and university presidents to attend the ceremony. The meeting began at 11:00 a.m. Those present included British Minister Cadogan, American Minister Johnson, Japanese Military Attaché Shibayama, Acting Chairman of the Military Branch Committee He Yingqin, Secretary-General of the Political Affairs Reorganization Committee He Qigong, Mayor Yuan Liang, Police Chief Yu Jinhé, Social Affairs Bureau Chief Cai Yuan, former Police Chief Bao Yulin, Minister of Railways Gu Mengyu, Special Envoy of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for Inspecting Ji, Jin, Re, Cha and Sui Provinces Jin Zhi, Speaker of the Peiping Municipal Council Lü Jun, Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce Leng Jiaji, Representative of the Banking Association Zhou Zuomin, Director of the Palace Museum Ma Heng, and Xu Songming, Li Zheng, Mei Yi-qi, Hu Shi, as well as over 400 Chinese and Western guests. German Minister Trautmann, Counselor Müllerre, Rosen, Secretary Wang Xudong, Wu Jiquan, and others were responsible for hosting. The German flag and the Nazi Party flag were hung high on both sides of the hall. Three pairs of white candles were lit on the stage, and many flowers and trees were arranged. The first ten rows below the stage were reserved for Chinese officials, rows eleven to thirteen for foreign envoys, and the remaining seats for Chinese and Western guests and newspaper reporters. After the funeral music was played, German Pastor Oelschlager officiated and led everyone in singing three memorial songs, which were very mournful. German Minister Trautmann and his wife were even moved to tears. Finally, a prayer was recited, and the ceremony ended at 12:07 p.m. Chinese and Western guests exited the hall in order. German Minister Trautmann and his wife, Counselor Müllerre, and Rosen stood at the door of the hall, and when Chinese and Western guests exited, Trautmann and others shook hands with each guest and thanked them. Minister Trautmann wore a full dress uniform and a black veil, and Mrs. Trautmann wore a black veil and black gloves. The ceremony was quite solemn. By 12:25 p.m., all the guests had left. (7th)

Northwest Inspection Report by Our Newspaper's Special Correspondent Geng Ya

Qing Province's Best Image is Not Planting Harmful Flowers

On the morning of the 26th, the weather was cold, and even wearing fur felt chilly. Departing from Zhangjia Town, the initial stretch was lined with elms and willows, providing shade, making pedestrians feel as if they were walking under bean and melon trellises. Villagers piled stones into pillars, ranging in height from four to five feet, numbering in the thousands. The tallest one had a wooden board inserted next to it, inscribed with the words: "Jade Emperor's Imperial Envoy Lei Chun, stopping torrential rain, suppressing demons," etc. Qinghai's high altitude weather, storms, and heavy rain are natural phenomena. With underdeveloped science, human effort is difficult to mitigate. Ignorant and foolish people then turn to the gods for help, which is the inevitable trend. If forests were cultivated on the four mountains, moderating the climate, the disasters of rain and hail could be reduced. In recent years, Qinghai has advocated afforestation on the plains, but has not considered the benefits and needs of planting trees in the mountains, which is truly regrettable. Qinghai's climate is dry and there is a trend of turning fertile land into desert. If human effort is used to save it, afforestation is the only way. Once the forests are established, they will conserve water sources and moderate the climate, which can be effective. Ten li to Baima Temple, where Hui, Han, and Tibetan people live together, totaling over forty families. Each teahouse and noodle shop has a village regulation posted, stating: "If there are disputes between Han, Hui, and Tibetan people, the fine is twelve yuan. Whether residents or pedestrians, if anyone sings songs near the village, they will be beaten one hundred and twenty times with willow branches." The temple is built against a steep cliff, its shape somewhat resembling the stone Buddha temple of Yungang. Suddenly, I saw over twenty Tibetan people, each holding wooden talisman stakes, and dog-head banners, etc., loudly beating drums and gongs, chanting the six-character mantra, circling the stone fortress three times, and shouting three loud sounds, then going elsewhere. I asked about their purpose, and they answered, "To ward off thunder, rain, and hail." At that time, Mr. Parr and Mr. Smith of the British American Tobacco Company were taking photographs. When they saw this, they asked me, "What country are they from?" I replied, "They are British." A Tibetan man seemed surprised and said, "Oh, are they the British from the After-Tibet side?" I replied, "Yes, are you afraid of them?" The Tibetan man said, "We are not afraid of the British or Americans, we only hate the Japanese, because Japan has seized our Northeast Provinces and Rehe, and also killed countless of our volunteers and civilians. Sir, I heard that Japan is only as big as our Sichuan Province. Then we can go and fight them. Ten people fight one of them, that should be enough, right?" I clapped to show my approval. He then asked me, "Sir, are you afraid of foreigners?" I replied, "Of course not." "If you are not afraid, why are you wearing yellow foreign shorts?" I was momentarily embarrassed, so I replied tactfully, "These are made of domestic materials, and I wear them while walking to keep cool. If you think the style is not good, I will change them in Xining." When they heard this, they shouted in unison, "Good, good, this is a patriotic compatriot." Then they dispersed with a hubbub. Nearby Tibetan people, because they live together with Han and Hui people, although they still believe in ghosts and gods, their knowledge of national affairs is not lagging behind, which is quite commendable.

Ten li to Caojiabao, and another ten li to Gaozhaibao, the terrain gradually rises, as if climbing a slope. Another ten li to Xiaoxiakou, where there is a bridge crossing the river, marking the boundary between Huzhu and Xining east and west. There are about ten families living on both sides of the bridge. The women wear bonnets, either black or white, similar to nurses and missionaries in hospitals. Those working in the fields wear white cloth sunhats, shaped like sieves, or simply wear scarves, which are also quite clean. The men mostly enjoy playing chess, or like to play hand-held games, even forgetting their farm work, and wasting their time on these two things. There is a small temple, dedicated to the Wind God and Rain Master, which is already badly damaged. Xiaoxia’s cliffs stand facing each other, thousands of ren high. The Huangshui River flows in the middle, its current swift and terrifying. The mountain path is narrow, and horses cannot walk abreast. The east is called "Xiaoxia Kou," and the west is called "Wangxia." If one defends this place, one person can be worth a hundred. If this is lost, the other places will inevitably be lost one after another. This is what military strategists call "fighting in a hole." Five li to the airfield, the field is wide and boundless. In the evening, I entered Xining City. In total, from Lanzhou to Xining, I traveled six horse stations, a total of 460 li. If traveling by car, detouring through Yongdeng (i.e., Pingfan), it can be reached in two days.

Qinghai was originally one of the frontier provinces. Although its culture is relatively backward, there are some good things I saw along the way that are worth mentioning. No opium poppies are planted within Qinghai. At a time when the Northwest provinces are financially exhausted and are competing to use opium poppy taxes as a means of generating revenue, Qinghai has not a single poisonous flower, which is truly commendable. If they can take it a step further, banning transportation and consumption, and benefiting the local people, it would be even more significant. This is its first good quality. Peaceful journeys, with tranquil villages, and major transportation routes, especially those where robberies are not likely to occur, is its second good quality. Water conservancy projects are distributed in various counties, greatly benefiting agricultural affairs. Its increased production and regulation of rural areas are more effective than other constructions, its third good quality. Qing Province's output of natural forests is very abundant, and it spares no effort in cultivating artificial forests. Everywhere, tall branches block the sun, and cool shade covers the land. If it can further extend to the cultivation of barren mountains, and the protection of natural forests, the future development of forestry will be even more limitless, its fourth good quality.

Communist Bandits Harass Southern Jiangxi

Bandits Hidden in Xunwu Annihilated

Bandits in Wuping Attempt to Seize Rice Crops and Suffer Losses

Guangzhou Communication: Communist bandits in Jiangxi Province have recently been rampant in western Fujian. At the same time, they secretly dispatched a force under Lin Biao to reinforce the line from Huichang to Yudu. Ye Jianying's force took the opportunity to attack Junmen. Lin Biao's force also moved west from Yudu, repeatedly invading the territory of Xinfeng. Therefore, the military situation in southern Jiangxi has suddenly become tense. Yesterday, Ye Zhao, the second division commander of the First Column stationed in Xinfeng, sent a secret telegram reporting the bandit situation in Yudu. Regarding the Second Column, after the Seventh Division repelled Ye's bandits who invaded Junmen Luotian at the end of last month, it has now stepped up its guard. According to a telegram from the Second Column headquarters yesterday, reporting the situation of bandit annihilation as follows: "According to an undated telegram from Division Commander Li Zhenliang, based on a report from Company Commander Qu Tingjian of the First Company: (1) About ten Communist bandits were discovered near Youyiejiao Market, five were killed on the spot, and three guns were captured. According to the division commander's telegram, relayed from Regiment Commander Wu Junsheng: Based on reports, a group of bandits fleeing from Dingnan hid in the Caodakeng area of Xunwu. The various battalions were ordered to dispatch a company to suppress them, but the mountainous forest was vast and nothing was found. They continued to search, and at about 3 p.m., a secret agent hired by our company reported that the entire group of bandits, numbering over a hundred, was indeed hiding in Danzhuping, ten li from Hejiao Market. As the 3rd Battalion was closer to that location, Battalion Commander Huang Shuguan was ordered to personally lead the search. A platoon was also dispatched from the troops stationed in E'zihu to intercept near Huangshashui. At 4 p.m., Battalion Commander Huang arrived at the location and made contact with the bandits, resulting in a fierce battle lasting about two hours. As a result, all levels of political commissars responsible for supervising the battle were killed, along with twenty-three bandits. Fifty-two bandits were captured. (Omission) The fleeing bandits are currently being pursued. Respectfully reported, Li Yangjing, respectfully kowtowing." Furthermore, according to a telegram from Huang Renhuan, the commander of the First Independent Division in western Fujian, based on a report from Regiment Commander Wu, over a hundred Communist bandits attacked Raoxi, about seven li east of Wuping, on the 25th, attempting to seize the farmers' rice crops. The regiment dispatched two battalions to encircle and suppress them. The bandits also stubbornly resisted, relying on the terrain. After three hours of confrontation, the Communist bandits began to flee into the mountains, with about thirty casualties along the way. Regiment Commander Wu has now returned to Wudong for guard duty. (August 4th)

Anhui Province

Establishment of a People's Food Adjustment Committee

丨Provincial Chairman Concurrently Serves as Chairman of the Committee丨

Anqing Communication: Anhui Province is suffering from severe drought with no rain, and the autumn harvest is hopeless. Dou Xiwén, the Standing Committee member of the Anhui Provincial Disaster Relief Committee, and others, recently sent a telegram to Duan Qirui, Xu Shiying, and Wang Yitang in Lushan, requesting them to appeal to Chairman Chiang for drought relief. The province also believes that at this time of severe drought, the people's food is the primary issue. In order to provide disaster relief and maintain the people's food supply, the Anhui Provincial People's Food Adjustment Committee is being organized, and the regulations of the committee have been drafted and passed at the provincial government's regular meeting on the 7th. The key points of the regulations are as follows: The committee will be composed of the following personnel: all members of the provincial government, the provincial party affairs commissioners, three members of the Anhui Provincial Disaster Relief Committee, and three members of the Anhui Provincial Rural Cooperation Committee. The chairman will be concurrently held by the provincial government chairman, and a vice-chairman will be concurrently held by a member of the provincial government. The committee will have three groups: general affairs, investigation, and adjustment, each with a director, selected from the committee members. The drought-stricken counties under the province should each establish a branch committee for people's food adjustment, with the county magistrate as the chairman and relevant personnel and local gentry as members. The drought-stricken areas under each county may establish a sub-committee for people's food adjustment, with the district head as the chairman and relevant personnel and local gentry as members. In the future, this will be beneficial to the regulation of the people's food supply. (8th)

Dispute Over Temples Used as School Buildings in Songjiang

The Fenglong Temple, adjacent to the Xichan Temple in this city, has been managed by the abbot of Xichan Temple, Monk Lanfeng, and used as a residence for monks. Last year, the principal of the nearby Public Second Elementary School, Zhang Yun, due to the increasing number of students and the insufficient school buildings, proposed to take over the Fenglong Temple and connect it to use as a school building. He submitted a report to the Education Bureau, which forwarded it to the Education Department for approval. However, the monks objected to this and filed a complaint against the Education Department's order. The Ministry of Interior ruled to revoke the original decision, and the temple was returned to the monks' management. However, Principal Zhang recently hired craftsmen to repair the temple and install doors and windows. The monk submitted a report to the county government to stop this. County Magistrate Jin, based on the Ministry's order, telegraphed the Education Bureau to stop the work. The school also reported to the Second Sub-Station that the monks had beaten two school workers, requesting the police to investigate. Police Inspector Lang dispatched Police Chief Qian to investigate. He only saw the monk Lanfeng tied up in the courtyard, with both sides holding to their own stories. He then sent both the principal and the monk to the County Public Security Bureau, which forwarded them to the court for review.

Famous Drug Trafficker Arrested and Sent to the County

Jin Zhao, a well-known trafficker of drugs and opium in Sijing, residing in the Dachang Clothing Store, was discovered by the Public Security Bureau. Special Agent Wang Yintang was dispatched with police to search the store, and a large quantity of morphine and opium was found. However, Song then summoned thugs to resist arrest and assault the police, and夺取证物, throwing the evidence out of the window and throwing lime, causing injuries to police officers Wang Qinming and others. Song escaped during the chaos. Wang returned to the bureau to report. Director He then dispatched Inspector Yan Jishi and Inspector Luo Junfen, along with detectives Xia Shengyu and others, to Sijing on the evening of the 7th, surrounding Song's front and back doors and entering the premises. Song was found lying in bed and was immediately arrested and taken back to the bureau. Inspector Luo then discovered that Special Agent Wang was suspected of taking bribes. Director He had Wang detained for questioning, and Wang confessed and returned twenty yuan in bribes. He has been sent to the county government for review along with Song.

Public Petition Provincial Authorities for Thorough Investigation of Land Tax Fraud Case

Regarding the land tax fraud case of Ye Zongcheng, the director of the First Land Tax Collection Office in this county, the county magistrate had Ye detained, as reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that Wu Baohuang, the supervisor of the special education funds of the province, believed that the tax revenue was of great importance to the education funds, and had requested Director Niu to investigate the case. Director Niu has now ordered County Magistrate Jin to provide a truthful report on the matter. The report from Supervisor Wu Baohuang stated that the county of Punán, after its paddy fields were converted to land tax, had been approved to reduce collection by 40% last year, and that the 18th year of the Republic was being collected in the 22nd year. In Pubei, the paddy fields converted to land tax were being paid off by the landowners year by year, which means that the paddy fields converted to land tax in Punán were also not entirely outstanding. However, Director Ye of the First Land Tax Collection Office, when reporting the autumn survey in the 22nd year, included all 119,000 mu of paddy fields converted to land tax in both Pubei and Punan under the outstanding tax item, encroaching upon the 60% of the tax revenue from the paddy fields converted to land tax in Pubei since the 18th year, and the tax revenue from the paddy fields converted to land tax in Punan that had already been paid since the 18th year, which was a very large amount. The county government has now appointed Yang Yunwen as the director of the First Collection Office, but has not thoroughly investigated Director Ye's encroachment of tax revenue, so a request for instructions has been submitted. The land tax of each county is related to the essential needs of provincial education. If the presented report is true, the loss to the special funds is very large and a thorough investigation and handling is urgently needed. The county magistrate is ordered to investigate why the paddy fields converted to land tax in Pubei were included with those in Punan under the item of outstanding tax. What are the actual facts? Did the former director embezzle tax revenue? A truthful report should be submitted immediately, along with a guarantee from the newly appointed Director Yang regarding the special provincial education funds, and submitted for review. (Omission) It is also learned that since former Director Ye was detained, he has been treated very well in terms of food and lodging, as he is already over sixty years old. It is said that the local public has submitted petitions to the provincial authorities requesting a thorough investigation.

New District Chiefs for All Counties in Suzhou Determined

After the Wu County government was ordered to merge with the autonomous region, the original twenty-three districts of Wu County will be merged into thirteen districts. All candidates for district chief have been determined and submitted by the county government to the Department of Civil Affairs for approval. The Department of Civil Affairs issued instructions yesterday (9th), and the following have been selected: Wu Erchang for the first district, Wang Deshou for the second district, Fu Zhaotang for the third district, Chen Yifei for the fourth district, Jin Jian for the fifth district, Zhu Shanqing for the sixth district, Qin Xigui for the seventh district, Shi En for the eighth district, Zhang Hong for the ninth district, Yin Suiyou for the tenth district, Tao Weigan for the eleventh district, Yan Yansheng for the twelfth district, and Zhu Liang for the thirteenth district. They will take over and organize the new district offices immediately.

Patrol Officer Xue Shoupeng Detained

Patrol Officer Xue Shoupeng of the Fourth Precinct of the Third Public Security Bureau was accused by someone to the Public Security Bureau of seven charges including dereliction of duty and bribery. After Director Wang confirmed the facts, he ordered Xue's dismissal. Subsequently, because a six-round pistol issued by the Public Security Bureau was sold by Xue, Director Wang was very angry and yesterday (9th) had Xue Shoupeng detained pending review.

Wuxi Southeast Transportation Expo Postponed

The Southeast Transportation Expo and the Joint Opening Ceremony of the Jiangsu Provincial Jiangnan Highways, originally scheduled for September 10th of this year, have been postponed due to insufficient preparation. It has been decided to hold it from October 1st to October 10th for four days, weather permitting. After August 25th, Shen Qi, the highway director sent by the Jiangsu Construction Department, will go to Zhejiang Province to discuss the Southeast Transportation Expo. The routes for the joint opening have been determined as the Jing-Wu, Jing-Hang, Xi-Yi, Xi-Hu, and Hu-Hang routes, and then from the Jing-Hang route to the Sheng-Ju, Zhen-Cheng, Xi-Cheng, Xi-Hu, Su-Chang, and Su-Jia routes. The Xi-Hu Highway is currently under active construction and is scheduled to be completed and open to traffic before the Double Tenth Festival. The road surface must be completed by the end of the year. Before the road surface is completed, it will not be officially opened to traffic. The Zhen-Cheng Road surface is scheduled to be completed before the Double Tenth Festival and officially opened to traffic. This road can connect with the Xi-Cheng Road.

Electricity Fee Dispute Escalates

The Xichang Qishuyan Power Plant of the Construction Committee recently changed its business regulations and notified its users that in addition to paying the meter deposit, they must also pay an additional electricity fee deposit according to the ampere of the meter. Upon hearing the news, the users believed that the Qishuyan Plant was increasing the burden on users, violating the purpose of national public utilities, and unanimously opposed it. Sun Xixia and others published advertisements to solicit opinions from all sectors of society. In the past few days, they have received three to four hundred letters contributing opinions from all sectors, all expressing firm opposition. Jiang Zhongliang, the chairman of the Hotel Industry Association, advocated organizing a united association of electric light users to firmly fight for their rights. The Qishuyan Plant sent a letter to the County Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating that it was not increasing the burden on users. However, it is heard that the reason for the plant's modification of the business regulations this time is that the current regulations require users who rent the plant's meters to pay a monthly meter rental fee in addition to paying the deposit, which is contrary to the Construction Committee's Electrical Business Regulations and is close to illegal exactions. Therefore, it is now planned to change it to an electricity fee deposit and return the meter deposit receipts. However, the users may follow the example of Peiping last year and jointly sue the plant in court for the meter rental fees collected over the years.

Provincial Government Implements Measures to Relieve Rural Areas

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs and Department of Finance, in light of the drought disasters in the counties south of the Yangtze River, urgently wanted to understand the true situation of grain reserves in various counties, and specially appointed Yu Bingdong and Zhu Yuwu to conduct thorough investigations in various counties. Yu and Zhu arrived in Wuxi on the 3rd and, together with County Magistrate Yan, carefully investigated the county's grain reserves and the exact amount of the two-five treasury bonds stored in each district, deciding to allocate four-tenths to purchase and store grain, and organize an Agricultural Warehouse Management Committee. They then went to Wujin and Jiangyin to investigate. It is now learned that the Department of Finance, in order to fully relieve agricultural production, has decided to implement effective relief work: (1) Pilot agricultural warehouse certificates; (2) Agricultural product storage pledge; (3) Agricultural product transportation and sales. The issuance of agricultural certificates in the first item will be piloted first in Wujin and Wuxi. Farmer remittances will also be handled. After implementation, the original Land Tax Office will be abolished and replaced by the warehouse for tax collection. Therefore, Yu and Zhu returned to Wuxi again yesterday. It is said that Jiangyin's disaster relief work has achieved the best results, so the disaster situation is lighter, and the grain reserves and funds are also the most abundant compared to other counties. Yu and Zhu have now gone with Gu Shuzhi, the president of the Farmers Bank, to Dongting to inspect the warehouses operated by the Agricultural Bank. As soon as the matter is completed, they will go to Suzhou.

Changshu Road Construction Causes Shopkeepers to Close

In this county, the construction of highways in various villages, particularly in the southeast region, has gathered hundreds of workers, mostly from other provinces. They often create disturbances on purpose. This has been a frequent occurrence since the road construction began. On the afternoon of the 7th of this month, a worker, Mr. Jia, from the Changtai Road construction project in Baimao Town, went to the market to buy two watermelons. A dispute arose over the price. Unexpectedly, the worker then led dozens of people back to the town. They first clashed with the watermelon vendors, and then started beating anyone they encountered. Because the workers were armed with kitchen knives and iron tools, no one dared to resist. The entire town was thrown into chaos, and shopkeepers closed their doors in protest. As a result, more than twenty villagers were injured, with Jin Xigen, Qian Chun, and the wife of the barber Gui Gui, suffering the most severe injuries. Later, the local defense corps attempted to mediate, but without success. Officials from the district office also fled in panic. The incident has now been reported to the county, and mediation is still underway.

Jiangyin Prefectural Commissioner Inspects Grain Reserves in Cheng

Finance Commissioner Zhu Yuwu, accompanied by Civil Affairs Commissioner Ding Bingdong, arrived in Cheng on the 7th to oversee the management of agricultural warehouses and investigate grain reserve funds, as well as the drought situation. After meeting with County Magistrate Bao and Chen Zhisan of the Farmers Bank, it was learned that over 10,000 yuan of Jiangyin's grain reserve funds remained. The Food Management Committee has already purchased over 5,000 dan of grain. They have now reclaimed the Education Bureau's buildings to expand the granaries, and will make further purchases after the autumn harvest. As for the drought situation, it is slightly better than in other counties due to its proximity to the river. It has been decided to first establish three agricultural warehouse locations in Houteng, Lujia Bridge, and West Stone Bridge. The two commissioners were scheduled to go to Wuxi on the 8th, rest for two days, and then proceed to Wu County for investigation.

Gaoyou Pig Boat Capsizes in Hurricane

Zhe Zilai, a pig merchant from Yigou Town in the first district of the county, purchased fifty-five piglets from Songjia Bridge in Huxi the other day and hired a boat to transport them. However, while traveling in the middle of the lake, they suddenly encountered a hurricane and the boat capsized. Fortunately, the boatman, Zhu, was familiar with the water and managed to rescue Zhe Zilai, preventing him from losing his life. However, the entire boatload of piglets was swept away by the waves, resulting in a loss of approximately 300 yuan.

Yangzhou Yu Family Embankment Nearly Collapses

The Yu Family Embankment in Xinyuan, the third district of the county, was in imminent danger of collapsing at 2:00 PM on the 8th due to a howling wind, torrential rain, and surging river tides. All the men, women, and children of the entire village gathered on the embankment at this moment, standing in the wind and rain, trying to protect the embankment. Fortunately, the hurricane and torrential rain subsided after ten minutes, and the embankment did not collapse. More than ten houses and large trees within the embankment were swept away by the wind and rain, making it a great stroke of luck amidst misfortune.

Xiaoshan Seventy-Year-Old Man Commits Suicide Due to Drought

In Xizhou, a southern village in Xiaoshan, there lived a farmer named Chen Jingchun, aged seventy. He had four sons, the eldest and youngest of whom were farmers, while the others were engaged in weaving. This year, the weather has been severely dry, and the eldest son died of illness on the 1st of this month due to exhaustion from drawing water for days. The youngest son alone could not manage the field work. The old man helped for several days, but the drought persisted without rain. He still had over twenty mu of land, which was completely withered. Because the weather was so dry and sunny, and the autumn harvest seemed hopeless, the old man cried bitterly for several hours on the morning of the 7th. In the evening, he drank a bowl of salt water and committed suicide. By the time his family discovered him, he had already died.
