Women's National Goods Movement Fair

Planning a Mobile Exhibition

Separate Mobile Exhibitions in Various Schools in the City

Collection of Products from Manufacturers Has Begun

The Shanghai Women's National Goods Year Movement Committee, in order to practice promoting national goods, has held various gatherings and established commercial fields to promote them. The association has decided to hold a mobile exhibition in various districts of the city starting in September. The details are recorded as follows:

Exhibition Regulations

Regulations of the National Goods Sample Mobile Exhibition

(Article 1) The name of this association is the National Goods Sample Mobile Exhibition.

(Article 2) The purpose of this association is to exhibit fine product samples from national goods factories to various schools in the city, to arouse students' awareness of national goods, and to guide them to deeply understand the value of using national goods.

(Article 3) The organizing group of this association is the Women's National Goods Year Movement Committee.

(Article 4) The organization of this association is divided into four departments: exhibition, speech, entertainment, and sales. Each department has a director who manages the affairs of the department. The methods are set separately.

(Article 5) The exhibition time of this association is temporarily set for one month, but it can be changed with the resolution of the organizing group.

(Article 6) This association is located in major and minor schools in the city. The address will be determined after contact.

(Article 7) The expenses of this association are assisted by the organizing group.

(Article 8) This association has a director who leads the overall process, and two staff members who handle all association affairs, who are appointed by the organizing group. The directors of each department are appointed by the director.

(Article 9) If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they can be temporarily revised.

Collection Method

The association's stipulated method of collection:

(A) The national goods samples collected by this association are classified as follows:

(1) Clothing and apparel

(2) Books and stationery

(3) Hygiene products

(4) Toys

(5) Food

(6) Furniture

(7) Musical instruments

(8) Sports equipment

(9) Daily utensils

(10) Other

(B) All exhibits of this association are collected from national goods factories and companies. All transportation costs are borne by this association.

(C) This association may request national goods factories and companies to select excellent products and send them to the association for display. The shipping costs for sending and returning the products are borne by the manufacturers themselves, and the handling fees during the mobile exhibition are borne by this association.

(D) All samples participating in the exhibition must indicate the name of the product, trademark, price, and the nameplate of the manufacturer should be affixed to the exhibit for identification (nameplates are issued by this association).

(E) This association is responsible for the safekeeping of all samples displayed at the exhibition. It is not liable for special losses.

(F) Anyone who wishes to participate in this mobile exhibition should first fill out a voluntary application, which will be approved by the committee of the organizing group before being allowed to join, and send the list of exhibits to this association before the deadline, and this association will issue a receipt. After the closing of the exhibition, the exhibits can be collected by presenting the receipt.

(G) The exhibition venue will be located in various schools in this city. The name of the school and the exhibition period will be announced temporarily in the exhibition schedule drawn up separately by this association.

(H) All factories and companies participating in the exhibition will be given commemorative certificates or souvenirs after the closing of the exhibition.

National and Foreign Goods Trademark Exhibition

Letter Requesting Collection by the National Goods Factory Association

The Shanghai National Goods Factory Association yesterday received a letter from the Preparatory Committee of the National and Foreign Goods Trademark Exhibition in Hangzhou, saying that the association, in order to increase the public's ability to distinguish between national and foreign goods and promote the effectiveness of using national goods, plans to hold a national and foreign goods trademark exhibition for two weeks starting on September 5. If the products can be borrowed for display, it will be especially welcomed. After the closing, they will be returned separately.

Male Corpse Floating in Puzhong Canal

At around 7:00 PM the night before last, an unidentified male corpse floated northward with the tide from the Pumi Canal in Yangshupu, to the area where the Customs Water Patrol Police Station was stationed. The corpse was spotted by a member of the police station, who hauled it up. The corpse was wearing a torn white twill short shirt, blue cloth pants, straight Gongni shoes with a floral pattern, no socks, and had a shaved head with a floral white hair band. It was estimated to be about 40 years old. Upon closer inspection, there were seven knife wounds on the head, with several of them deeply penetrating the skull. Considering the case involved injury, the police chief was notified. Upon inspection, it was determined that the deceased was likely stabbed to death with a knife and then the corpse was thrown into the Puzhong Canal to try to cover up the traces. However, the corpse had not yet decayed, and it was estimated that it had been in the water for only about ten days. Yesterday morning, Chinese detective Huang Songsheng was ordered to transport the corpse to the Lifesaving Bureau and report it to the local court. After reviewing, Prosecutor Xiao confirmed that the deceased had been murdered and ordered the bureau to collect the corpse and instructed the police to strictly investigate the murderer and handle the case.

Jealousy and Adultery Lead to Corrosive Liquid Attack

Ding A'si Suffers Serious Injuries

Ding A'si, a 24-year-old Yangzhou native residing at No. 123, Lane 171, Wangzhi Road in the French Concession, works as a shop assistant at a Westerner's house and lives comfortably. Yao Wenmei, a young woman from Huiyang of about the same age, possesses a bit of beauty and a romantic nature. She also works as an amah at the same Westerner's house. However, due to the lack of confidentiality, Sha Ziming, Wenmei's former lover, found out and was consumed by jealousy, plotting revenge. Yesterday morning, around 7:00 AM, Ding and Yao Wenmei were passing near the Xiejiao General Assembly Hall on Jing'an Temple Road when they were suddenly ambushed by Sha Ziming, who was lying in wait by the roadside. When he saw the two approaching, Sha rushed up and splashed a bottle of corrosive liquid on Ding's head. At that time, Ding A'si was caught off guard, and his head and face were covered in corrosive liquid. Immediately, his skin was torn and flesh was rotten, a terrible sight to behold. The perpetrator, seeing that his goal had been achieved, quickly ran away without a trace. Wenmei, seeing the great disaster, also fled westward. Ding immediately hired a rickshaw to go to Baolong Hospital for treatment. It is said that his injuries are serious, and his life is in danger.

Rent Reduction Association Sends Letter to Lawyers

Cases Rejecting Rent

Separate Letters to Sun Xinyuan and Yiyuan Company

The Rent Reduction Committee of this city yesterday sent a letter to the Shanghai Lawyers Association, requesting it to inform its members to refuse to accept rent disputes. The original letter stated: "To Whom It May Concern, we have recently received a letter from the Xicheng Lane Tenants Association of the French Concession, stating that the houses in which they live, a total of 134 households, have been rented for more than ten years. They have been managed by Yipin Bank and have rental contracts and agreements. Unexpectedly, this year, Yilian Company has taken over the management. When the company took over the management, it stated to the tenants that it was a change in name only and that there would be no other changes. Unexpectedly, within three months, the company ordered them to sign a new contract. Because the tenants found the contents of the new contract to be quite harsh, they dared not accept it and requested modifications. Unexpectedly, the company hired lawyer Wu Zhenming to sue them for refusing to sign the contract in the First Special District Court. After the people clearly defended themselves to the court, they were judged to dismiss the plaintiff's lawsuit. However, the company was still unwilling to give up and filed an appeal. The rent in Xicheng Lane was increased by 10% in 1930. Now, with the economic downturn, it is really unbearable to bear this huge amount of rent. Please grant relief," and so on. Since the "January 28th Incident" until now, all industries in Shanghai have been in decline to the extreme. The reason for this is the high cost of rent. Landlords not only do not consider reducing it, but also exert pressure, causing the citizens to suffer no less than during the "January 28th Incident." In this situation, if we do not find a way to deal with it, how can we maintain the people's livelihood and revive the market? After thinking it over and over, we can only ask your association to inform its members to refuse to accept rent disputes, so that the landlords will have no way to use their skills. In the future, the market will be able to recover, and the people's livelihood will be worry-free. We are grateful for what your association has done. We believe that the gentlemen of your association understand the market situation and will certainly not be happy to follow their lead. Therefore, we are sending this letter according to the situation. Please investigate and handle it."

Unexpectedly, within three months, the company ordered them to sign a new contract. However, the company was unwilling to give up and filed an appeal. The rent in Xicheng Lane was increased by 10% in 1930. Now, with the economic downturn, it is really unbearable to bear this huge amount of rent. We are sending this letter to ask for your assistance to maintain the people's livelihood," and so on. Based on this, since recent years, all industries have been in decline, which can be said to have fallen sharply. All moral landlords have successively initiated voluntary rent reductions, which are published in various newspapers every day. I think you have already understood it, and there is no need to repeat it. Taikoo Company

Northern Line Liners Offer Special Treatment to Passengers

Hiring Armed Guards to Protect the Ship

The Taikoo Company's Northern Line has three ships, Shuntian, Shengjing, and Tongzhou, which sail between Shanghai, Weihaiwei, Yantai, and Tianjin. The Shuntian and Shengjing are new ships with fast speeds, so they also stop at Qingdao. It only takes twenty-four or five hours to reach Qingdao from Shanghai. In addition, the ships are well-equipped and the cabins are comfortable, so passengers say it is convenient. After the Shuntian was robbed by pirates in Dagu in June, the company proposed to equip the three Northern Line ships with anti-theft iron gratings for the safety of passengers to prevent unfortunate events from happening again. It is currently requesting instructions from the London headquarters. In the past, the company was very strict with passengers, requiring reliable guarantors. Also, because ticket agencies were not allowed to sell passenger tickets on their behalf, passengers expressed dissatisfaction, which greatly affected business. The company realized the reason and changed its plans, seeking to develop rapidly. For the safety of passengers, it hired many armed guards to protect the ship. All travel agencies and ticket agencies can still sell passenger tickets on their behalf, and the ship's purser's office has also resumed selling tickets to facilitate passengers.

Orphanage

Announcement of the Continuation of the National Child Welfare Conference

Outline of Measures Enclosed

The Chinese Child Welfare Association has been very busy recently preparing for the National Child Welfare Conference. Letters have already been distributed yesterday, along with an outline of measures, excerpted below: (Conference Dates) October 10th to 13th, 1934; (Location) Shanghai; (Attending Representatives) (1) One or two leaders of child welfare organizations selected by the Civil Affairs Departments of each province and the Social Bureaus of each city; (2) Leaders of charitable organizations in various regions whose work is related to child welfare; (3) Specially invited child education experts and pediatricians from various regions; (Conference Proposals) Any agencies or organizations that send representatives, or individual representatives, or agencies that cannot send representatives but wish to submit proposals, are requested to send them directly to the Chinese Child Welfare Association at No. 131, Museum Road, Shanghai before September 15th of this year; (Representative Expenses) Travel expenses for representatives attending the conference shall be borne by the agencies or organizations or individuals they represent. However, the association can request the Railway and Communications Departments to issue discounted fare certificates, which will be sent out for use before the conference. All expenses within the conference venue will be borne by the association, and accommodation expenses may also be arranged by the association as appropriate; (Soliciting Exhibits) Before attending the conference, representatives from various regions are requested to collect children's achievements, as well as the regulations, reports, photographs, statistics, charts, etc., of local child welfare institutions, and mail them to Shanghai as soon as possible for use in the Child Welfare Exhibition held simultaneously with the conference. For exhibits that are inconvenient to mail, they can be brought to Shanghai when attending the conference.

Riverbeds Dry Up, Manure Boats Suddenly Decrease

Cleaners in Zhabei in a Panic

Gathered at the Labor Union Yesterday to Petition

Requesting the Authorities to Find Ways to Provide Relief

The excrement of citizens in Zhabei has always been purchased and transported by farmers from the interior by boat. This year, due to the collapse of the rural economy, the fertilizer business has plummeted. In addition, since the summer, there has been a severe drought, and riverbeds have dried up. The number of manure boats arriving at the port averages only one or two per day, resulting in an abundance of material but a shortage of boats, making transportation impossible. Moreover, the city has no facilities for storing fertilizer. The sudden decrease in manure boats has made the work of cleaners extremely difficult. If they do not work, where will the waste from the millions of households be dumped? If they do work, where can they unload the fertilizer? If they dump it in ditches or the Huangpu River, they will be fined by the police. The cleaners of Zhabei are at a loss as to what to do in the long run. Therefore, yesterday afternoon, a crowd of sixty or seventy people gathered at the Sixth District Cleaners' Union, demanding reasonable negotiations: (1) Requesting the municipal authorities to set up an agency for storing fertilizer so that fertilizer can be stored when there are no boats; (2) Before setting up such an agency, please actively find ways to increase the number of boats; (3) The wages of porters have always fluctuated depending on the number of boats. Now, due to the lack of boats, their income is only three or four yuan per month, making it difficult to make a living. They demand that fixed wages be set according to the original conditions.

Two Roads Bureau

First Discussion Meeting of the Research Office

Both Director Huang and Deputy Director Wu Gave Speeches

The staff of the Research Office of the Two Roads Bureau held their first discussion at 10:00 AM on August 8th in the conference room. Except for researcher Wang Qiguang, who was absent due to official business, all other members attended. First, Wang Renshouzhi, the head of the office, reported on the organizational process and invited the director and deputy director to provide instructions on the direction of the work.

Director Huang's Speech: (1) The reason for establishing the Research Office is to solve important, special, or complex problems in the bureau's administration, operations, and technology, in order to increase efficiency and develop the business; (2) The organization of the Research Office involves selecting personnel with knowledge, experience, and a strong research spirit from various departments. They should conduct research on various issues in a practical and humble manner. All researchers are part-time and will not receive additional salary. It is definitely not a sinecure for accommodating personnel; (3) The designated office location is currently temporarily located in the surplus space of the Materials Department. In the future, it is planned to open three rooms near the General Affairs Department and the Machinery Department, with one room as an office and two rooms for relocating the library to facilitate research; (4) Visiting other agencies to study their research work and facilities. The Bank of China in Shanghai, the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, and Jiaotong University all have research offices or institutes. Although their nature is different, we can first visit these places for observation and investigation to learn from them. In the future, we should also go to the South Manchuria Railway Research Institute for inspection within the economically feasible range to collect ideas and broaden our perspectives; (5) Research Standards and Scope: Conduct research in accordance with Articles 7 and 8 of the regulations, taking each event as a unit, exploring its historical, factual, legal, or economic relationships, and formulating concrete methods for improvement or resolution. The scope of research does not involve the powers and daily routine matters of various departments, nor does it hinder the duties of researchers in their respective departments; (6) Research Methods: Scientific methods must be adopted, and attention should be paid to the three points of truth, goodness, and beauty.

Deputy Director Wu's Speech: (1) It is hoped that Director Huang will pay special attention to the organization of research work in railways or other agencies in various countries during his overseas inspection, and collect as much material as possible for reference by the bureau's Research Office; (2) It is hoped that the Research Office staff will work hard during the overseas inspection period and make considerable progress. Finally, all researchers and attending staff exchanged opinions and decided that regular weekly discussions would be held every Thursday at 9:00 AM without further notice. Proposals should be submitted by researchers in advance and compiled by the director for the agenda, which will be presented for discussion at the meeting in order to start the research.

Fudan University Student

Verdict in the Case of Du Nanxi's Murder

Zhang Asi, a native of Suzhou, along with Xiao Wang, who is at large, ambushed and murdered Du Nanxi, a Fudan University student from Sichuan, in front of No. 47, Puchun Lane, Marlborough Road, in the French Concession, at around 8:00 AM on March 24th of last year. The French police searched for them but were unable to capture them. Later, Zhang and his accomplices, Lu Jiaxiang, Zhu Tianming, and Ma Boli, natives of Ningbo, were arrested for committing robbery in the International Settlement. The First Special Court sentenced Zhang to fifteen years of imprisonment, Lu to twelve years, Zhu to ten years and six months, and Ma to twelve years. The sentences were confirmed and they were sent to prison. Recently, Zhang suddenly discovered his conscience in prison and confessed to the Du murder case. Jin Jiulin, the Inspector-General of the French police, along with detectives Zhang Ziying, Zhou Buguang, and bao detective Cai Jinzhang, learned of this and brought Zhang to the French police station for investigation. They learned that in addition to killing Du Nanxi in the French Concession, Zhang and his three accomplices, Lu, Zhu, and Ma, had also committed robbery. Lu Jiaxiang had also agreed to the murder of Du at the time. Therefore, Lu, Zhu, and Ma were also brought to the case and sent to the Second Special Court to be prosecuted for crimes such as murder and robbery. Chief Judge Wang Gangxu concluded the trial and awaited sentencing. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday was the date of the verdict. Chief Judge Wang presided over the First Criminal Court and sentenced Zhang Asi to fifteen years of imprisonment and fifteen years of deprivation of civil rights for aiding and abetting premeditated murder. The robbery charges were dismissed. Lu Jiaxiang was sentenced to three years and six months for carrying a weapon and gang robbery, reduced from five years for carrying a weapon and gang robbery, to be served for seven years. Zhu Tianming was sentenced to five years for carrying a weapon and gang robbery, reduced from seven years for carrying a weapon and gang robbery, to be served for eight years. Ma Boli was acquitted. After the sentences were announced, the defendants were transferred back to the detention center to await further instructions.

Reading Q&A

Continued "Errors and Difficulties in Translations" (Ran Xu)

丨Reply to Mr. Du Luoji丨

Question: "The decline of the capitalist system is not due to the laws within that system, but must be the conscious work of the working class." The last sentence is unclear.

Answer: This translation is slightly different from the original text, which should be translated as: "The decline of the capitalist system is not due to the laws within that system, but must be the conscious work of the meaning of the working class. Hilferding separated the meaning of the working class and their conscious actions from the contradictions of capitalism and class struggle." "The conscious work of the meaning of the working class" means that it is not necessarily caused by social contradictions, but rather something that the working class does according to their own meaning and intention.

Question: "... it has an unchanging divine right to demand a share of the utopian lion," please explain.

Answer: This sentence should be translated as: "It has an unchanging divine right to demand a share of the utopian spoils." The original translation is incorrect. "To demand a share of the utopian lion" should be translated literally as "to demand a share of the utopian lion." "The lion's share" means the food that the lion can snatch. What the lion snatches is of course a lot, so it can also be translated as "spoils." This sentence can be translated more colloquially as "... it has always had a large part of it that is utopian."

Question: The paragraph from page 197, lines 9 to 12, where Marx criticizes Feuerbach, is very unclear.

Answer: This sentence means that Feuerbach can only see the things of each era in each era, but does not understand the developmental relationship between one era and another.

Question: "... not towards filling abstract thinking with the content of political decrees, but towards dispersing the content of existing political decrees and treating it as abstract thinking." Could you explain the two aspects in a more colloquial way? (To be continued)

Free Talk

On the Employment Problem of Young People

— Bai Ge

In the midst of the worldwide unemployment panic and economic downturn, the employment of young people naturally becomes a problem. Undoubtedly, the main focus of this problem is not whether young people are willing to work, but rather that there is simply no work available. Therefore, our investigation of this problem can only find its causes from an objective perspective, and not from the young people themselves. However, recently, some people do not regard this problem as a serious social problem, but only see it as a phenomenon caused by the unconsciousness of young people, and blame the young people. For example, Mr. Youmo is one such person.

Mr. You's article "The Employment Problem of Young People," published in "Free Talk" the day before yesterday (August 6th), begins by saying: "Is there a way out for young people? This question seems difficult to answer at first glance. Because from a theoretical point of view, it can involve major issues such as social ills, landlord exploitation, and the collapse of the rural economy. If we expand further, we can extend this to serious topics such as the economic aggression of the great powers, the world's economic downturn, and the decline of the imperialists. But abandoning theory and talking about facts, I feel that the problem of young people's way out is not as serious as mentioned above. Whether they have a way out or not, the key lies entirely in the young people themselves; in other words, it depends entirely on whether they can be conscious." Then, he cited several examples to prove that the reason why young people are unemployed is entirely because they "are unwilling to compromise" and "prefer to turn down opportunities," proving that "they clearly have a road ahead, but they refuse to take it." Finally, he affirmed a conclusion: "Therefore, do young people have a way out? On this question, I dare to prove with facts that they cannot say they have no way out, but they have gone in the wrong direction."

Mr. You's meaning is very clear: as long as young people can be more frugal and not "think about material comfort or high pay," they will not be unemployed no matter what kind of work they do. If we use the examples cited by Mr. You, as long as middle school graduates do not want to be postal workers, compradors in foreign firms, bank managers, or section chiefs and commissioners, and are willing to compromise and become elementary school teachers with a monthly salary of twenty-two yuan or even manual laborers, the number of unemployed people in society will naturally decrease day by day. However, Mr. You has not considered that society does not lack elementary school teachers and manual laborers with monthly salaries of twenty-two yuan or less, and they are also just as crowded and experiencing an unemployment panic. Even if the general student population follows the path pointed out by Mr. You, the result will simply be to squeeze out another group, those who have had fewer opportunities to receive education and have not achieved a higher status, turning those in employment into the unemployed and simply swapping their positions. Can this be considered a way out for young people? Do those young people who have not received middle school or higher education not need a way out? Does their widespread unemployment not become a problem?

The Chinese have always advocated diligence and frugality for building a career, and Mr. You himself is among the general middle school and higher students, so he only came up with such a way out for the youth graduated from middle school or above. This is originally not surprising. We only hope that Mr. You can take a break from the circle surrounded by students and open his eyes to look at things outside of students, to see if the problem of young people's unemployment or whether they have a way out is really "can involve major issues such as social ills, landlord exploitation, and the collapse of the rural economy" and "can also be extended to topics such as the economic aggression of the great powers, the world's economic downturn, and the decline of the imperialists," and not let the young students around him block his own eyes. To take a step back, Mr. You should at least look beyond the little bit of facts he cited as examples and see what kind of significance the recent graduation of students from various universities in Beiping and the rise of the vocational movement represents.

Impressions of Zibo

— Luo Wang

(VII) The Blind with Bright Eyes

The fate of miners often leads to "hanging themselves from the southeast branch" [suicide due to poverty and hardship]! However, looking at it from another perspective, there are also material goods workers! Glassblowing workers! Their end often turns them into beggars—the blind with bright eyes!

As reported earlier, besides coal, the next most important product of Boshan is "Boshan Glass" and "Boshan Material Goods."

Indeed, Boshan's glass, glass silk mirrors, and material goods, with their exquisite carvings and bright colors, are enough to outshine Western goods! In the past, Germans who came here to travel would buy Boshan goods and admire them as antiques! A pair of vases often fetched prices of a hundred, fifty, or thirty yuan. Foreigners had plenty of money! Boshan merchants made a lot of foreign wealth!

Many glass and colored glaze products rely on workers blowing them! Therefore, these workers, responding to the demand for goods, worked extra hard, breathing near hot furnaces every day, focusing their eyes only on the objects they were blowing! Over time, after decades, all their time was spent beside the melting furnace, and their eyesight gradually became nearsighted! Eventually, they became white-eyed! They couldn't see clearly unless the object had extremely strong luminosity! Furthermore, their eyes were injured, and in old age, they became the blind with bright eyes! Unable to work, unable to eat, they ended up becoming beggars!

Since the Northeast Incident, the sales of Boshan material goods have decreased! As a result, fewer workers are employed, and the furnaces are not always lit! In this way, it seems that many workers' eyes have been saved! However, another problem has followed: the unemployment and wage reduction of glass workers! This phenomenon, many elderly Boshan people can recount! The vicissitudes of life are truly lamentable!

New Talk on Old Subjects

— Yu Shixia

| A Look at Popular Language Literature from a Historical Perspective |

No matter how good your advertisement is, if there are no goods to show people and immediately prove your claims of low price and high quality, then your words are lies and nonsense—this is something everyone can say.

"Bring out the goods!" This one sentence can shut the mouths of those who boast about their goods without substance.

Do you advocate for popular language? Do you support the construction of popular language literature? Then please show us some examples of popular language. This request isn't too excessive. | However, it's a bit like seeing a single chicken egg and treating it as a rooster, hoping it will crow at dawn—somewhat impatient. In reality, the masses are just the masses; they aren't gods who have fallen from the sky. As long as you have ears, you can hear the voice of the masses; as long as you have eyes, you can see the face of the masses. Aren't the people you interact with and deal with every day the masses? You yourself are also a part of the masses, as long as you are considered a person. Saying it this way, popular language is the language of the masses—does that need to be said? Popular language is what the masses can speak, understand, write, and read, and that can also represent the progressive consciousness of the masses. Such language and writing should be called popular language—who would disagree? Classical Chinese doesn't meet this standard, so it's certainly not popular language. Is vernacular Chinese popular language? This needs to be discussed separately.

First, let's talk about ancient vernacular literature:

Existing ancient vernacular literature should be traced back to the *bianwen* of the Tang and Five Dynasties and the *pinghua* of the Song Dynasty. What was the popular language of the Tang and Song Dynasties actually like? We don't really know. Since the *bianwen* and *pinghua* of that time were spoken by storytellers and understood by the masses, we can consider them the popular language of that time without being too wrong.

Next, let's talk about poetry. The poems of the Tang Dynasty monks Wang Fanzhi and Hanshanzi used vernacular language and were very popular among the people. A Tang Dynasty manuscript of Wang Fanzhi's poems was discovered thirty years ago in the Dunhuang grottoes. Hanshanzi's poems were inscribed on rocks, and people wrote them on the walls of their halls. They used the language of the masses to write poems, propagating the philosophy of life they had learned from Buddhism. These kinds of poems were able to circulate among the people because they were like maxims, from which one could gain some lessons; if they hadn't been close to the vernacular language of the masses, no one would have paid attention to them, even if the lessons were good. As long as it's close to the vernacular language of the masses and can grasp the psychology of the masses and cater to the tastes of the masses, it can still circulate among the people, even if there are no lessons or even if it's the opposite, and shouldn't be taken as lessons. A little before Wang Fanzhi and Hanshanzi, Yang Junzhi of the Northern Qi Dynasty wrote many six-character poems, which were said to be very lewd and very shallow, and circulated among the people under the name "Yang Wu's Companions." Some people copied and sold these songs, and they were available in every market. Once, Yang Junzhi was passing through a market and saw a written copy of these songs, with mistakes in them. He wanted to correct them for the person selling the copy. The seller said, "Yang Wu is an ancient sage. How could there be mistakes in the companion songs he wrote? What do you know, daring to spout nonsense?" Unfortunately, Yang Wu's Companion songs haven't been passed down, otherwise, we could see what kind of tunes Li Jinhui was making 1,900 years ago. Isn't the reason why Mr. Li Jinhui's songs are so popular everywhere today still due to the two elements of shallowness and lewdness? Although these songs use a language close to that of the masses, their content only caters to the lower tastes of the masses and doesn't represent the progressive thought of the masses, so they are still far from ideal popular language songs. In short, whether it's Yang Wu's Companions or the poems of Wang Fanzhi and Hanshanzi, setting aside the content, they were willing to oppose the literati of the time and insisted on writing in the colloquial language of the masses of that day, which is also commendable.

Speaking of poets who used popular language, we can think of Bai Juyi of the mid-Tang Dynasty. It's said that he would read a poem he wrote to an old woman, and he would only be satisfied if the old woman could understand it. His New Yuefu poems were very sympathetic to the laboring classes of the time, and they fiercely scolded the plundering and tyrannical nature of the aristocratic officials—the ruling class. He set four principles for himself when writing these poems. The first principle was to make them easy for people to understand. The second principle was to make them move and awaken people when they read them. The third principle was to use realistic materials for the subject matter, the current political and social problems, so that people would believe what he said was true when they read them. The fourth principle was to make them easy to turn into songs and set to music. Originally, he thought that poetry must have four fundamental elements: language, emotion, thought, and sound, so he set these four principles for writing poetry. Sure enough, his poems were successful and achieved the greatest effect of poetry during his lifetime. He saw that from Chang'an to Jiangxi, for three or four thousand *li*, his poems were inscribed everywhere, and everyone was reciting his poems. Some people were writing his poems to sell for money or to give as gifts. From cities to villages, from princes and high officials to cowherds and grooms, everyone could hum his poems. It can be imagined how widely his poems circulated! At that time, Yuan Gu and Liu Yuxi were good friends of his, and their poetic styles were similar. Being willing to use ordinary vernacular language to write poems, daring to write poems satirizing the authorities, and being able to imitate the form of folk songs to write poems—these were the characteristics of the Bai Juyi school of poetry at that time. In short, they liked to use the language of the masses and write about the lives of the masses to create poetry, and the masses also liked to read their poems or sing their poems. They can truly be said to be the greatest popular language poets of that era.

I Come from the East (19)

— Xingye

Along the roads at night, were piles of idlers with nothing to do, still humming songs like "Drizzling Rain." Shop entrances hung with bizarre and outlandish signs, and under the electric lights, twos and threes of shop assistants leaned against the doorways, aimlessly watching the street; their way of leaning was especially particular: bellies sticking out, necks drooping down, and sometimes their right foot crossed behind their left. When speaking or singing, they moved their chins. Some even shook their heads as they sang. Most of them were small and thin, with long gowns hanging on their bodies, turning their bodies into a reed pipe. All of this, after three years of absence, particularly caught my attention.

The hotel smelled strongly of pungent opium smoke. There were people playing cards in the next room, and someone was arguing in the middle of the night. Shanghai people are truly skilled at arguing, as if insults have been prepared under their tongues, and once their tongues are unleashed, it's like a tap turned on, flowing endlessly. I wanted to interfere with them, but I was afraid of being scolded myself. Looking down at the road from the high building, it was still full of people. They walked very slowly, and their hands swung back and forth like windmills.

The rickshaw pullers of three years ago were still bending forward and running fast, and the Indian "Ah San" of three years ago were still stretching and bending their left and right hands. Although North Sichuan Road had changed its appearance, the air of North Sichuan Road was still the same. We ate dinner at New Asia, and the fancy-loving Cantonese brought out an unknown menu; we ate something called "Planting Jade in Lantian" and "Jade Xishi," but we still didn't know what Xishi was made of. We Chinese are truly particular about what we eat, but we don't pay much attention to what happens after we eat it.

Shanghai has been placed before me, and China has been placed before my eyes, and I am about to begin my new adventure. At the center of this world's great upheaval, I can see the dangers, greatness, intensity, illusion, chaos, passion, and cruelty ahead. I silently looked out the window, watching the dim and unclear starlight filling the sky, fantasizing about myself and China in five or ten years. (The End)

Night Records from the Borderland (Middle)

— Wu Yan

The door opened, and the old woman's face, still bearing traces of fear, appeared in the dim light of the vegetable oil lamp, with a pitiful expression. The man who had been speaking was nowhere to be seen, and judging from the tone of his voice when he spoke to the old woman, he could only be considered a stranger. Immediately, I thought, what does he do?

The old woman probably thought I was a kind person, so she gently patted her chest and turned her eyes in gratitude to a painted image of Guanyin Bodhisattva on the wall.

I had just sat down and was washing my feet in a wooden basin when a brother from the merchant escort team barged in, wearing a military cap on the back of his head and carrying a foreign gun in his hand. He rudely shouted:

"Old fellow, lend me a bedsheet to use, quick, quick!"

The old woman was so frightened that she couldn't speak and retreated, leaning tightly against the mud wall.

This impolite brother rummaged around the room, grabbing a small plate of buckwheat kernels placed in front of the Guanyin Bodhisattva and stuffing it into his mouth.

"Oh dear, that's offered to the Bodhisattva!"

The old woman cried out in a gasp, raising her old hands like withered vines and scratching her hair wildly.

"Offered to the Bodhisattva? Good, let this living Bodhisattva eat it!"

He ate the buckwheat kernels and joked with the old woman, while his feet kept moving around the room, and his eyes kept darting around the corners of the room.

For some reason, he suddenly started arguing with someone in the inner room. The other person's accent belonged to the man I had heard speaking at the door earlier.

I sat still, just washing my feet, and heard the man speaking inside, seemingly still stomping his feet.

"This old mother only has this one sheet, only this one sheet..."

"Old fellow, do you want to get physical? Good—come on!"

*Slap*—a sharp, crisp sound of a slap echoed, followed by the man's loud wail.

"Hey, you dare hit people randomly? Recognize me! Recognize me! I'm not some country bumpkin!..."

"Oh dear, Heavenly Grandfather, Heavenly Grandfather!"

At the same time, the old woman was also crying out in a hoarse voice.

I quickly and carelessly slipped my wet feet into my straw sandals, and before I could tie the straps, I rushed in to see, wanting to do my best to mediate.

At this time, the man had already come out wrestling with the merchant escort team brother. He was not yet forty years old, but his beard was already very long, and even the hair by his ears was preserved as part of his beard. Therefore, his appearance looked even more solemn. If he were wearing a Taoist robe, he would look very much like an old Taoist priest. He shouted as if he were blowing his beard:

"Go see the captain, go see the captain!"

Sports News from the Javanese Overseas Chinese Football Community

Planning to Invite Domestic Football Teams to Campaign in the South Seas

The Delegation Will Be Dispatched by the Far Eastern Games

(Special Dispatch from Batavia, this newspaper) Overseas Chinese love sports, almost as a natural inclination. Throughout the South Seas, wherever there are Overseas Chinese, there are sports associations, and they often hold the leading positions in local sports such as football, tennis, volleyball, basketball, and badminton. Even Westerners who are fond of sports cannot compare with them. The "Zhonghua Qunli Sports Association" organized by the Overseas Chinese in Batavia, the capital of Java, has a large number of talented people and excellent skills. It is not only the best in the Dutch East Indies, but also compares favorably with major ports in China. For example, the nationally renowned football star Li Huitang was formerly a mainstay of the association. In addition to participating in inter-port competitions and international competitions in various parts of the South Seas, Qunli frequently invites famous domestic teams to compete in the South Seas. The most notable examples are the expeditions to Java by the Lehua and Nanhua teams many years ago. At the end of last year, the association once again contacted Mr. Yu Hengzhi, the former leader of Lehua, to discuss reassembling the old team and contacting the elite of the South China football community to campaign in the South Seas. Just as everything was ready and the expedition was about to depart, it was suddenly prevented by other reasons, and the trip did not take place. The Qunli Association was very frustrated to hear this. Recently, in order to implement its objectives, the association has again sent letters to domestic teams, asking them to campaign in the South Seas again. It is said that letters and telegrams are being exchanged, and negotiations are underway with various parties. As for which domestic team will represent the country, it is not yet known. However, according to another source, the Chinese team that won the championship in the Far Eastern Games in which our country participated this time will come to the South Seas. If this can become a reality, it will not only revitalize our motherland's national prestige in the South Seas, but also make the general football fans dance for joy.

Shanghai Inter-Port Tennis Tournament

Performance in Nanjing

Lin Baohua Defeats Ma Shaobo

Zheng Zhaojia Defeats Pan Liwei

(Nanjing, 9th dispatch) Lin Baohua, Zheng Zhaojia, and others, at the invitation of the Amateur Sports Association, came to Nanjing for a performance on the morning of the 9th. In the afternoon at 4 o'clock, the performance was held at the association's court. Seating was set up on both sides of the court, and tickets were sold for one yuan. More than 400 spectators attended, and Zhu Jiahua, Tang Shengzhi, Chu Minyi, and others also came to watch the match. There were two singles matches. Lin Baohua vs. Ma Shaobo, two sets to zero, Lin wins. Zheng Zhaojia vs. Pan Liwei, two sets to zero, Zheng wins. There was one doubles match. Lin Baohua and Liang Deguang vs. Zheng Zhaojia and Pan Liwei, two sets to one, Lin and Liang win.

In the first game of Lin Baohua vs. Ma Shaobo, Ma served first. The serves were as heavy as cannonballs, resulting in a tie. After repeated attempts, Ma was finally defeated by Lin. Ma lost again in the second game. After Ma won back one game in the third game, Lin won all four games. Lin won both the first set six to one and the second set six to two.

In the singles match between Zheng Zhaojia and Pan Liwei, Zheng served first. Errors occurred repeatedly. Zheng lost the first game five to seven. Afterwards, each had wins and losses. Zheng then won three consecutive games, winning the first set six to four. In the second set, Zheng's momentum became stronger. He first won two games, lost two games, and then won again six to three.

In the doubles match, Lin and Liang defeated Zheng and Pan in a very exciting show. Lin's stability and Liang's activity, Zheng's left and right attacks were often effective, and Pan's high kill on the net was especially superb. Lin and Liang also won the second set seven to five. In the end, two sets to one, Lin and Liang won.

Three more matches will be held today. On the 10th, there will also be one singles match, Lin Baohua vs. Carlson, and two doubles matches, Liang Deguang and Huang Jixiang vs. Yu Zhizhong and Zhao Minheng, Lin Baohua and Zheng Zhaojia vs. Pan Liwei and Carlson. Lin and others will visit the mausoleum on the morning of the 10th, and Chen Ce will host a banquet in the evening, and they will return to Shanghai by night train.

The Shanghai Municipal Council is Planning to Build

An Open-Air Swimming Pool in the Western District

South of the Singapore Park

Expected to Open in the Summer of Next Year

The Health Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council prepared a budget this spring to build new dressing rooms next to the Hongkou Park swimming pool. After review by the Works Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council, it was deemed that the area was already extremely crowded, and it would be better to build a new pool than to expand the existing site. Therefore, it was decided that a new pool site should be considered this year, and the Director of the Works Department was requested to prepare a plan. It is now learned that the Director of the Works Department has prepared a drawing for a swimming pool to be built at the southern end of the Singapore Park, and it is planned to start construction at the end of December this year or in January next year. The construction cost is included in the 1935 budget, so that the pool can be opened in the early summer of next year. It is reported that this proposal has been adopted by the Board of Directors of the Shanghai Municipal Council.

Nanjing Women's Middle School and Elementary School

To Be Renamed Zhenjiang Experimental Elementary School of Jiangsu Province

Entirely Moved to Zhenjiang in Three Years

Enrollment to Cease in Nanjing This Year

Because the Normal Department of Nanjing Women's Middle School will be completely finished with this class, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education decided some time ago to rename the Provincial Nanjing Women's Middle School Experimental Elementary School to the Provincial Zhenjiang Experimental Elementary School, and to move it entirely to Zhenjiang in three years, ordering the school to comply. After receiving the order, the school decided to first establish the lower grades of the elementary school in Zhenjiang after the summer vacation this year, temporarily using the Zhenjiang 53 Library as the school site, while constructing a new school building. The Nanjing school will be renamed the Nanjing Branch of the Jiangsu Provincial Zhenjiang Experimental Elementary School. For the convenience of completion, the original lower grades of the Nanjing school will be merged into two combined grades, while the remaining middle and upper grades will temporarily maintain their original status, but enrollment will cease, with the aim of gradually completing the relocation to Zhenjiang within three years, in accordance with the Department's order. For the convenience of communication, all official documents and letters will temporarily use the Nanjing Branch as the hub.

World Student Association

Held a Conversation with International Students Yesterday

Zhu Shaoping Reports on Travel Precautions

Student Group Organized, Wang Yukai and Others Appointed as Committee Members

This year's students going abroad are scheduled to depart on the 14th and 21st of this month on the President Hoover and President Jackson liners. The World Chinese Student Association held a conversation with international students yesterday afternoon at 4:00 p.m. to discuss travel precautions and the organization of a student group. The details are as follows:

Students Present

Wu Youliang, Wu Youlin, Wang Kaiyu, Gao Qian, Zhou Shoumin, Wu Zaidong, Huang Wenxi, Peng Qixin, Li Zhennan, Cheng Zongqiao, Qin Kuan, Zhou Qingxiang, Wu Shu, Zhou Shiping, Zhu Lancheng, Wang Jiazeng, Lei Junmin, Sun Shengzeng, Xu Beiming, Hu Minjie, Hao Lüduan, Yang Shangzhuo, Lei Zuowen, Ling Zhaolin, and more than forty others were present. Except for two students going to the UK, the rest are going to the US.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Zhu Shaoping reported, stating roughly that since everyone is going abroad for the first time, they are naturally unfamiliar with travel matters. In recent years, the US has been rejecting Chinese laborers, and the restrictions on Chinese entering the country are very strict. A little carelessness can lead to unexpected suffering. The first thing to pay attention to is health issues, such as eye diseases, etc. The second is luggage and books, as the physical examination and luggage inspection of Chinese entering the country are particularly strict. As for Chinese products, such as tea and silk, it is not advisable to bring too much, as bringing too much will raise suspicion of being a merchant and will also be restricted. The journey from China to the US takes three weeks, so there should be a systematic organization of life on board. In addition to casual conversation, the organization of a student group is also very necessary today, etc.

Organization of Student Group

After the Chairman's report, the organization of a student group was discussed. Wang Yukai, Wu Youlin, Yang De'en, Yang Shangzhuo, Qin Jing, Lu Jiqing, and Peng Qixin were appointed as committee members of the President Hoover liner student group, with Wu Youlin as the chairman of the committee. Zhou Qingxiang, Wang Jiazeng, Sun Shengzeng, and Lei Zuoyun were appointed as committee members of the President Jackson liner student group, with Lei Zuoyun as the director of the committee. After the meeting, a photograph was taken and refreshments were served before adjourning. It is said that the students going abroad this time will all be issued letters of introduction by the World Student Association to be given to European and American classmates for hospitality.

Su Hongbin, Lin Qiwen, and other representatives of the National Jida Vocational Sports Association who are going to Beijing to petition have departed from Shanghai yesterday with a petition and are heading directly to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Education to petition. It is reported that the association's petition is divided into three points: (1) Request the Ministry of Education to instruct Principal Shen to earnestly rectify school affairs, carefully select professors, improve the school's status, and not to dismiss the old and employ the new, and exclude students. Chinese Institute of Engineers Gives

Methods for Honorary Gold Medal

Academic organizations in Europe and the United States often have methods for awarding honorary gold medals or medals to people who have made special contributions to construction undertakings, in order to encourage academic experts to concentrate on construction undertakings, either to seek improvement for the country and society, or to create happiness for mankind. The intention is extremely good and beautiful, so the country is becoming richer and stronger, and talents are emerging in large numbers, and all industries are prosperous, not because they are good at rewarding and promoting them. The Chinese Institute of Engineers, in view of this, passed the method of awarding honorary gold medals at the conference last year, which was handed over to the board of directors for execution. Now, on June 24, the 14th board of directors meeting passed seven articles on the method of awarding honorary gold medals. Those who receive honors are not limited to members of the association, in order to be popular, but are limited to engineers of Chinese nationality. The seven articles of the method are listed below: (1) The association may award honorary gold medals to people who have made special contributions to the engineering community in accordance with this method. (2) The honorary gold medals of the association are temporarily set as one type. (3) Those who receive honorary gold medals must be Chinese citizens, but are not limited to members of the association. (4) The standards for special contributions to engineering are as follows: (A) Invention: (1) Those who have new theories in engineering; (2) Those who have mechanical items or manufacturing methods that benefit mankind and national defense; (B) Those who are responsible for presiding over huge projects and solving technical difficulties to achieve success. (5) Any Chinese citizen who meets the standards of Articles 4A and 4B may be proposed in writing by more than ten members of the association and submitted to the association. After approval, the two departments of directors and executors shall hire five experts to form a special committee to review it. (6) If the review result is confirmed by the board of directors to be in compliance with the provisions of Articles 3 and 4 of this method, the association will award the honorary gold medal at the annual meeting every year. (7) If there are any matters not covered in this method, the board of directors may revise it at any time.

Spring and Autumn

Record of the Vague Aroma of Imperial Incense

— Original by Princess Der Ling of Qing, Translated by Qin Shouou

After clarifying this point, she then issued many orders, sending the eunuchs to carefully arrange the many antiques and jade artifacts hanging on the walls of the carriage. It seems that she was still not satisfied with our method of display, so she did not hesitate to come up with her own ideas and rearrange them again. After the changes were satisfactory, she looked at it herself and felt that there was nothing to criticize, so she ordered the carriage to start. In addition to these antiques and jade artifacts, she expressed her full satisfaction with all other decorations and arrangements, such as murals, curtains, vases, carpets, etc. Therefore, her spirit was more excited than usual. Although she was almost seventy years old at that time, her face was full of complacent smiles after getting on the carriage. She pointed east and west, and was as happy as a seven- or eight-year-old child who had received a new toy. Among them, the point that made her feel the utmost complacency was that on this special train, the authority of the Empress Dowager was revealed more clearly than elsewhere, and the impact was particularly swift. As long as she hummed in a low voice, the entire train would move forward, backward, or stop. At the same time, this small court of hers could move at will on the land she ruled without any effort. In the eyes of people at that time, it was indeed a very proud thing!

Before I entered the palace, not only had I taken countless trains abroad, but I had also taken several trains in my own country, and I did not feel anything different. Only this trip made me feel extremely nervous from the very beginning, even when preparing. From beginning to end, I was always holding two handfuls of cold sweat, fearing that some unexpected disaster would happen. Because the Empress Dowager had never seen a train, perhaps the various actions of the train would inevitably be displeasing to her. In this way, there would be no peace on the road! What worried me especially was the initial jolt when the train started. This jolt would of course have no impact on others, but it could not be said for the Empress Dowager. (102)

An Old Tea Drinker's Humor

— Mei Xue

Drinking *ban cha* (slab tea) is a specialty of us Suzhou people, and so is telling humorous stories. Someone said, "After drinking *ban cha* for three years, even someone who isn't humorous will become so." These two sentences are quite true. The gentlemen who are qualified to drink *ban cha* are generally very good at sitting still. Some hold a cigarette, smoking one after another; others slowly draw on the water pipes that are not seen in Shanghai but are still popular in the inland areas of the spring and autumn period, puffing tube after tube. They wear an unhurried and calm expression, enjoying listening to others talk while not opening their mouths much themselves. When they do speak, their tone always contains a hint of teasing. This kind of tone was called "pure conversation" in the Jin Dynasty and is called "humor" in modern times.

I am a young man who likes movement and not stillness, so naturally, I am not qualified to drink *ban cha*. Occasionally, during a break, I would invite classmates to a tea house for a bowl of tea. We would always joke with each other, never stopping for a moment. The old gentlemen drinking *ban cha* then gave us a nickname, calling us "rush teenagers." I thought of a saying, "A rush cannot be used as a walking stick," and went to ask the old gentleman, "You say we are rush teenagers, are you mocking us for being useless teenagers who cannot support a heavy burden?" The old gentleman flicked a piece of paper and slowly said, "That's not necessarily so. What I said was 'climbing-and-noisy teenagers.' You climb to that place and make noise in that place. Aren't you climbing-and-noisy teenagers?"

Another day, I happened to mention in the tea house, "I just saw a group of people outside drinking 'mediation tea,' banging on the tables and benches, even venting their anger on the teapot, punching it and breaking the teapot's spout." As I was speaking excitedly, this old gentleman interjected with a cold remark, "How can you say it's venting anger? They should knock off the teapot's mouth." I couldn't help but laugh and asked him the reason. The old gentleman finished smoking a tube of pipe tobacco, exhaled two streams of white smoke from his nostrils, and slowly said, "It's just because that mouth talks too much, argues too much, so it should be knocked off."

I have been ridiculed twice by the old gentleman. He is a senior, and I cannot argue with him. From then on, I kept a vigilant heart and dared not go to that tea house for tea again.

Zhenhai Tower in Lingnan

— Qing Lin

In the northeastern part of Guangdong's provincial capital, there is a street called "Dashitou." It was once a district where music gatherings were abundant but is now renamed Yuexiu Road. West of the street is a mountain, called Yuexiu, also known as Baiyun, commonly called Guanyin Mountain. Halfway up the mountain is the Guanyin Temple, a place where pious men and women offer incense and pray to Buddha. It is rare to see a mountain within a city, and in its towering magnificence, it displays an extremely upright and refined charm. When Hong Xian (Yuan Shikai) claimed emperorship, Long Jiguang controlled Lingnan, obeying the Northern Court. It was not until the Revolutionary Army launched a joint attack that he fled to Hainan Island. Even in isolation overseas, he continued his separatist rule for a year. Initially, Li Xiehe led the armies of Fang Shengtao and Zhang Kairu to attack Guangdong. Long Jiguang was unwilling to give up his territory immediately, so he plundered the people's wealth and stubbornly resisted. He built fortresses on Baiyun Mountain and constructed a flying bridge directly to his headquarters. The sturdiness of the construction and the perfection of the equipment truly made it the most formidable defense project in terms of tactics. Remnants still exist to this day. Chen Jitang even learned from his old tricks, expanding and improving upon them. Therefore, today's Guangzhou has fortresses in all four suburbs.

At the peak of Baiyun Mountain, there is a towering building that rises high into the sky. The Cantonese people commonly refer to it as the "Five-Story Building." Its actual name is "Zhenhai Tower," an ancient building dating back thousands of years. It is believed to have been built by Zhao Tuo, King of Nanyue. On fine spring days, tourists climb to the top floor, overlooking the entire city's scenery, which is all within sight. In the distance, the Pearl River is visible, with sails and masts standing like a forest. The Humen fortresses, embracing the mountains and facing the sea, can also be vaguely seen. According to legend, although it has been repaired over the generations, its foundation remains extremely solid and unwavering. The walls, bricks, and tiles have been well-maintained, demonstrating the meticulous craftsmanship and the quality of the materials used in its construction. The entire building's beams and pillars are made of top-grade *nanmu* (Phoebe zhennan), with the main pillars being square-shaped and large enough to be embraced by arms. There are four of them, standing at the four corners of the southeast, northwest, and southwest. According to traditional Chinese architecture, the center of gravity relies on the pillars. As this is a five-story building, if the pillars were slightly weak, they would not be able to bear the load. In the late Qing Dynasty, there was a fire that almost caused it to be burned down. The guard of the tower tried to blame it on "heavenly fire" to shirk responsibility. Superstitious people echoed this, adding various embellishments, leading to all sorts of absurd and baseless stories. However, it is a pity that this giant pillar was scorched by the fire! I remember when I was a child in Guangdong, I loved to climb it on holidays. Now, it has been twenty years since I returned to my hometown. When I read Han Gaozu's line, "The great wind rises, the clouds fly," I couldn't help but feel a long-lost yearning!

The Four Northeastern Company Commanders

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 32: Generals Indulge in Pleasure All Day, Soldiers Return Amidst the Weeping of Young and Old

Just as he reached the second gate, he saw Gan Jizhi and a nurse in white talking there. He was startled when the nurse called out, "Mrs. Zhao, who are you here to see?" As soon as she spoke, Guizhi recognized her as Huang Manying. She didn't know how she had ended up working as a nurse in such a place. She nodded and said, "Long time no see." At the same time, he turned his head and nodded to Jizhi. Jizhi's face was red, as if he was embarrassed. But he immediately realized that this was a solemn place and couldn't act like a lover. He put on a serious face and said, "Mrs. Zhao, are you here to see Company Commander Yin and ask about the whereabouts of Company Commander Zhao?" Guizhi said, "Yes. But Company Commander Tian, Company Commander Guan, they all..." She couldn't go on. Her throat tightened, and she choked. Jizhi said, "I work as a secretary here. I admire Company Commander Yin. I've talked to him several times and know the situation on the battlefield. You don't need to be sad. Company Commander Zhao..." Before he could finish, Huang Manying gave him a couple of winks. Jizhi had no choice but to stop himself. Guizhi had already seen it clearly and asked, "He... he... is he dead?" Manying said, "Don't worry. Let me take you to the waiting room to sit down, and then Jizhi will take you to talk to Company Commander Yin. In any case, you have to take care of yourself." As she reached out to support her, Guizhi saw an engagement ring on her hand. She immediately looked at Jizhi's hand and saw a similar ring. She thought to herself, at this moment, she was facing eternal separation from her husband, while others were enjoying marital reunion. By contrast, it made her even more heartbroken. Just then, a new batch of severely wounded soldiers arrived, being carried into the hospital on stretchers. This made her think of Zhao Ziqiang's situation. She felt extremely desolate but couldn't cry out loud, so she fainted and fell. Fortunately, Jizhi was quick and immediately caught her. In this desperate moment, she had at least fallen into the arms of her lover. But militarists would surely say, "For the wife of a soldier, this kind of outcome is very common." (453) (End of the book)

Pawnbroking

— Hua Ling

Although banks also accept collateral and engage in lending, those who seek loans from banks must have documents such as deeds, mortgages, stocks, government bonds, or valuable jewelry like diamonds to even be considered. Therefore, in Shanghai, although there are all kinds of banks—foreign, Chinese, large, and small—and countless of them, pawnbrokers and pawnshops, which are as densely packed as scales on a fish, are still thriving despite charging higher interest rates than banks.

Although pawnbrokers also accept collateral and engage in lending, pawnbroking is much more accessible to the common people than banks. In pawnshops, anything can be pawned. Gold rings and ivory chopsticks can be used as collateral, and even long gowns, short jackets, and trousers are considered good collateral. Items worth one or two hundred dollars can be pawned, and items worth three or five cents can also be sent to the high counter behind the white walls for a quick loan. It is said that in the Luandong area, some pawnbrokers run by foreigners even accept living people as pledges. This is indeed a new record in the history of pawnbroking, but accepting dumpling carts and cold noodle stalls as pledges is very common in Shanghai. In short, anything that is worth a few dollars and is not a completely useless piece of junk will be accepted by pawnshops.

Therefore, people generally call pawnshops "maternal uncle's home," meaning they can be consulted in times of emergency. Although pawnshop interest rates are at least 1.8% per month, and small pawnshops can charge as high as 3%, this is not considered exploitative profiteering but rather a service to the people. Therefore, pawnshops always hold the position of "maternal uncle's home."

Miscellaneous Chat

A Treasure Among Men (Part 2)

— Tian Xu Wo Sheng

"The patient underwent surgery without feeling any pain, and recovered within a month. I never truly believed in Hua Tuo before, but seeing Dr. now, I believe that there are indeed people with miraculous skills in the world. Out of gratitude and admiration, I recount the experience to inform others with the same ailment, and to record my unforgettable gratitude!" This matter occurred five years ago. The preservative solution I used was initially salicylic acid, which was not durable. Later, I switched to boric acid glycerol, which remains intact to this day. After more than forty experiments, none could dissolve it. Only lightly oxidized potassium could slightly dissolve it. I realized that lightly oxidized potassium cannot be ingested, but heavy potassium bicarbonate can. Therefore, I made a solution of heavy potassium bicarbonate and added gallstones. After adding a small amount of tartaric acid, I saw it immediately start to boil, and the gallstones became active, appearing thinner. I took them out and weighed them on a chemical balance, and they had lost 3% of their weight. After repeating the process once more, they lost another 3%. After a total of thirty-four trials, they were completely dissolved. From this, I learned that heavy potassium bicarbonate is indeed a symptomatic medicine that is not difficult to take. Its taste is salty and slightly astringent, and the dosage can range from 0.5 fen to 1 qian. One fen can dissolve in 3 fen of water, but tartaric acid tastes extremely sour and is difficult to swallow. I realized that there is already acid in the stomach, so it is acceptable to drink grape wine. Therefore, I first stored dilute hydrochloric acid in a test tube to simulate stomach acid, added a small amount of grape wine, and then added gallstones. At this point, there was no reaction. When I added heavy potassium bicarbonate, it started to boil and digest more quickly. Taking it a step further, I tried the principle of mutual sensation between substances. I used gallstones as a guide, finely ground them, and mixed them with heavy potassium bicarbonate, storing them in capsules. I still simulated stomach acid as above, added grape wine, and then added the capsules, heating them to 37 degrees Celsius. Sure enough, they digested very quickly, and they were able to dissolve completely in just fourteen trials. Thus, I understood that I could cure the same disease. However, there was no one with this disease available to be tested. In September of the *ren shen* year, the daughter of my relative Mr. Gu was diagnosed by a doctor with stomach cancer that could only be cured with surgery. Mr. Gu did not dare to try surgery, and as they decided to go to the hospital for surgery, his daughter cried and said she would rather die than go. I tried it as a test. The daughter was good at drinking wine, so I added acid to the grape wine and provided it for her regular consumption. She drank it three times a day, each time about two *liang*. I supplemented it with the aforementioned capsules, three each time. One capsule's dose was 1 gram. Soon after taking it, she burped, and her chest and stomach felt much more relaxed, and she urinated a lot. Fearing that it would enter the bladder or turn into stones, I used an artificial Carlsbad salt method to change the heavy sodium bicarbonate to potassium and introduce it into the large intestine, excreting it through the feces. She gradually recovered, and because she returned to her hometown to sweep the tombs, she asked for a month's worth of medicine. A New Year's card came, saying that she had long been completely cured and had not relapsed since. She drinks three glasses of grape wine every day, and her appetite is also healthy. Now, she is married and has children. She is stronger than ever and has no illnesses all year round, probably because the iron in grapes can replenish blood. The amount of gallstones used was very small. The total amount was only 90 grams. If calculated using the price of *mabao* (horse bezoar), the retail price in pharmacies is 2 yuan per *fen*, so each gram would cost more than 5 yuan, which is also considerable. However, compared to hospitalization and surgery, the medical expenses are thousands of yuan or more, and the family suffers from fear and anxiety, as well as caring and nurturing for half a year, the cost of which is even more incalculable. Mr. Wang said it was a treasure among men, which is an ideal statement, but based on the facts, Miss Gu was saved by it. It can almost be said to be a treasure for saving lives. There are herbs called human yellow and human white, so it is appropriate to call it a treasure among men, isn't it?

Financial News: U.S. Government Vigorously Purchases Silver

Spot Gold Plunges Again and Again

Falling for Ten Consecutive Days Without Rebound

Yesterday's Market Dropped Another 10 Yuan and a Half

Nearly Breaking the 50 Yuan Mark

The gold market has been consistently weakened by the U.S. government's continuous purchases of silver. Yesterday, the market nearly broke through the 50 yuan mark. Although the situation stabilized midway, the buying side was discouraged and inactive, leaving a bleak outlook. At the start of the morning, overseas silver markets reported that London and New York both rose, with the five-metal exchange's forward silver price rising nearly one fen and far rising three li and a half. London gold rose two and a half pence, exchange rates had rebounded, American cotton rose 45 pounds, American wheat rose 8.75, and stocks also rose. Market sentiment was still good. Although the opening price of gold fell, it was not much, dropping to 57 yuan. Hengyu, Yuqing, Yongfu, Xingyong, Yifeng, Yongda, Decheng, and others sold, and it continued to fall within 5 yuan. After the opening, although the bank's appetite was reduced, due to the lower prices, buyers were eager and the price rose, but there were many pullbacks. The HSBC listing revealed that the British pound rose 1.25 and the U.S. dollar rose 0.25. At this time, market sentiment was stable, and the price fluctuated, which was quite annoying. Later, the Central Bank opened with spot purchases, and the buying momentum in the market turned surging, and the gold market once became strong. However, the selling side was unwilling to show weakness, and supply increased after the price rose, and the market situation remained weak. However, the banking market was flat, and the balance of power between buyers and sellers was balanced, and it seemed to hover. The situation was generally stable, but under the threat of overseas silver markets, buyers were naturally cautious, while sellers were the opposite. Therefore, the underlying trend was ultimately weak, and Reuters' comments on silver by two London companies, due to the U.S. government's vigorous purchases, would inevitably rise sharply. The rumors were even worse, and the decline became even more severe. After the noon close, it once broke through the 50 yuan mark before stabilizing. The after-market was stable due to the Reuters report that U.S. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau would announce today that silver imports exceeding 100 yuan must have a certificate from that country. The bank bought again, and it rebounded.
