Shanghai Newspaper Local Supplement

Small Talk

A Few Idle Words on Mr. Jiawei's Critique of a Smaller Problem

— A Long

The day before yesterday, I wrote an article, "A Few Words on Several Minor Issues Raised by Mr. Cao Regarding the Popular Language," which was published in the supplement. This caused a misunderstanding with Mr. Jiawei, who also wrote "A Review of a Smaller Problem in the Discussion of the Popular Language." Naturally, he expressed deep dissatisfaction with my opinions. But is my mind just dull and slow, or is it because I lack ink in my belly? The more Mr. Jiawei critiques, the more confused I become.

Mr. Jiawei's rebuttal to my article is divided into four points. However, these so-called four points are vast in meaning and mixed in ideas, with repeated errors, making a comprehensive debate impossible. I can only casually point out the points of Mr. Jiawei's misunderstanding and correct them. Therefore, the writing inevitably becomes too long, causing the editor to have a headache, and taking up a large portion of the valuable space in the supplement, just like the Japanese occupying a large area of territory for no reason. I am deeply sorry for this.

The original text states (i.e., the following is from Mr. Jiawei's original text): "Everything in human society will never be freely transcended by you beyond history, and the generation and development of this problem are determined by objective historical conditions."

Indeed, the occurrence of all events is always subject to objective historical conditions. Even the transition from classical Chinese to vernacular Chinese has historical characteristics. Confucius said, "Just make the meaning clear." Li Bai's and Du Fu's poems, which even old women could understand, were also intended to be simple and clear. Zhu Yuanzhang of the Ming Dynasty said that ancient people wrote to clarify morality, communicate worldly affairs, and the words of ancient books were all clear and easy to understand. Nowadays, scholars write only to convey principles and clarify worldly affairs, without using flowery language. Later, Mr. Tang Shunzhi more clearly advocated vernacular Chinese. This is a historical fact. During the May Fourth Movement, people like Hu Shi and Chen Duxiu advocated vernacular Chinese, but in fact, they were only expanding and enriching the sayings of Song Dynasty scholars, the colloquial stories of the Song Dynasty, and vernacular literary forms such as "Water Margin" and "Dream of the Red Chamber." In reality, there was not much creation. This is based on historical evidence. Therefore, Confucius said, "The Yin dynasty inherited the rites of the Xia dynasty, and what it subtracted and added can be known. The Zhou dynasty inherited the rites of the Yin dynasty, and what it subtracted and added can be known." It can be seen that history is "gradual" and not "sudden." If people today, seeing Hu Shi and others making a splash, also want to play around with a popular language, I'm afraid it will be more effort than it's worth.

The original text also states, "In today's society, due to the contradiction between productive forces and production relations, there is continuous development, and the popular language is an inevitable product of the social trend towards collectivization."

According to Mr. Jiawei, each era has its own products: classical Chinese for the monarchical era, vernacular Chinese for the republican era, popular language for the current era, and perhaps something like Cheng Yaojin becoming a Grand Marshal for a later era – a big circle for merit, a big stroke for demerit.

The original text also states, "The term 'the masses' must represent the masses who can bear the mission of historical development and the progress of the times and can move forward."

This is originally a representative system. The general public naturally cannot bear such a significant mission, and those who can are naturally a few gentlemen with eloquent tongues and eyes like copper bells. However, representative systems, such as the former advisory councils, national assemblies, and provincial assemblies, have also had such a set of tricks. In the end, there was only bribery, fighting, table-flipping, and ink-throwing. Representative systems are only like this. The current representative system has been in chaos for a long time, and I can't see any achievements. What is the reason?

The original text also says that the popular language and popular literature cannot be discussed separately. Anyone who pays a little attention to philology knows this. Popular literature is not something that has only been proposed today. A discussion and production of it occurred a long time ago.

I have my reasons for advocating separate discussions. Mr. Jiawei ignores my reasons, which is like fitting a cow's head to a horse's face, and then says that there has been a discussion and production of it. Forgive my ignorance, I have heard of the discussion, but I have not seen the production. I don't know what the produced popular language is like? And since it has already been produced, why is there a need to discuss it again at this time?

The original text also says, "The popular language proposed today only needs to be something that can be written, understood, and spoken."

Such language seems very convenient: if you can write it, you can hear it; if you can hear it, you can speak it. There is no need to discuss it carefully. I'm afraid this kind of language cannot be created by human power. Only God can create it. However, after God created the world in six days, He needs to rest on Sunday. I'm afraid He doesn't have the energy to create a popular language for us again?

The original text also says that the construction of the popular language will become the simplest, most widespread, and complete tool for educating the masses; and the construction of popular language and literature, along with other departments such as popular films and dramas, is relatively raising the cultural level of the masses.

What I want to study is what kind of tool this is: an ax, a chisel, a hoe, or an iron rake? What is the form of this tool? The popular language has not yet been produced, but movie theaters and theaters already exist, which is strange. And to say that the cultural level will be raised in these places is even stranger. Now things are only following the masses. Why do we need to raise their culture? I didn't know where the popular language was before. Now, thanks to Mr. Jiawei's guidance, I have found it – it's in movie theaters and theaters! I am really happy. However, the popular language in theaters and movie theaters is raising the level of the ladies, mistresses, young masters, and young ladies, not raising the level of the general laborers, coolies, and farmers.

The original text also says that there has been a lot of discussion on the problem of discarding and developing dialects and localisms in the construction of the popular language, so there is no need to say much about it here.

Why is there no need to say much about it here? This is the most serious core of discussing this issue. Because the discussions from all sides have not produced practical and good solutions, it is truly as Mr. Cao Juren said, "There is only the clamor of gongs and drums, but no officials appearing on stage." Therefore, we need to discuss it. But Mr. Jiawei says that there has been a lot of discussion on all sides, so there is no need to say much about it. According to this, Mr. Jiawei's long article of several hundred words is also redundant.

I have read several of Mr. Jiawei's articles in the supplement and deeply admire them. But this article is very contradictory in content and avoids practical discussion, only circling on the surface, which is incomprehensible. I have already written a lot here and cannot go into further detail. However, since Mr. Jiawei has joked about my flawed writing, I cannot help but say a few words and make a joke as well. If Mr. Jiawei thinks this is an insult and becomes very angry, and then writes another review, I cannot handle it. I can only give a warning and ask Mr. Jiawei not to get angry.

From Bound Feet to Women's Liberation

— Tian

In the past, judging the beauty of a woman depended entirely on the size of her feet. Three-inch golden lotuses were the standard of beauty. Thus, beautiful women swayed like willows in the wind, with light and graceful figures, able to do nothing but burn incense under the moon and play the xiao in front of the window. A pair of small feet was also deeply hidden within the silk skirt, unwilling to be easily shown to others. Those with a fetish for feet, the most famous in history, were the great massacres that took pleasure in piling up small feet.

Now, in 1934, the high tide of women's liberation resounds to the skies, and the red silk ribbons of the foot-binding woman no longer evoke a sense of beauty in people. On the contrary, the bigger the feet, the better. One can run dozens of miles and jump several feet high (although one also puts on high-heeled leather shoes and twists and sways when running into the dance floor, this is another matter and not worth mentioning). A pair of feet like footboards can jump and bounce, earning the respect of martial artists.

This is not a matter of the superiority or inferiority of size, but a matter of different times. In the era of small feet, people risked their lives to bind them with foot-binding cloths that were several feet long. In the era of large feet, people run, jump, leap, and climb walls. The former was because women were confined in the towers of feudalism, and they had to do this to win the favor of men. The latter are awakened women who have shouted slogans such as women's liberation. Naturally, forging a healthy physique is the first step towards liberation. They are unwilling to be accessories to men under the yoke of economics, and they want to compete with men in society and politics. However, time is like a golden hoop. After several women's liberation movements, they broke free from the old chains, but were invisibly imprisoned by new chains. Although their feet have grown larger, they have not obtained what they hoped for.

According to the import surveys of cosmetics and lace, the daughters of the era of large feet have only overthrown the painful sacrifice of three-inch golden lotuses. They are still trapped in this golden hoop like Sun Wukong.

As the saying goes, "Those in the midst of a situation are confused, while those on the sidelines are clear." This saying has some truth to it. Small-footed girls simply do not know the status of women. If small feet are the standard of beauty, then they grit their teeth and make them smaller. And there are even songs praising their merits, saying "From now on, all parents in the world will not value sons over daughters," covering their eyes and running into the maze, not knowing what they have been doing until their beauty fades and they die. Now, their feet have grown larger, and the slogans they shout are very fashionable. Seeing men as enemies, and if someone says "vase" or "signboard," they launch a naval, land, and air force attack, earning a paper victory of gender equality. In reality, they are also spinning in the maze, but this time they are doing it with their eyes open, embracing the ambition of "If I don't go to hell, who will?" to become heroes. But think about the taste of eating mute pills with your eyes open.

After writing this, I know that I have caused another great disaster. However, I am not waving a feather fan to make a "borrowing arrows" deal. These past two days, reading the newspapers has made me feel a bellyful of frustration. I want to ask the big-footed girls to jump out of the maze and take a look at the people applauding and cheering on all sides!

Lamenting Han Juntianfang

— A Ping

It seems to have become a fashionable trend for literary figures to be valued after their death. Today, upon receiving Mr. Chen's letter of condolence for Weinong, I learned that my friend Tianfang had passed away on July 1st. I couldn't help but feel sad for a long time. Upon examining my stationery cabinet, I still have two unpublished manuscripts. Because they have lost their timeliness, they can't be published. I originally could have added the words "posthumous works" to give my friend a little posthumous fame. However, Han Jun has a spirit, and I know that he would definitely not want to do this. I will just casually discard them and end this case. What use is it to have glory after death when literary figures have nothing to eat when they are alive?

I met Tianfang at a dinner party last autumn. He was employed in the editorial department of the World Book Company. This spring, he was transferred to the second editorial department in Suzhou. We had only been together for less than half a year, and our last meeting at the newspaper office became our eternal farewell. The conversation at the time of parting seemed to be a prophecy of his departure.

That afternoon, he came to the editorial office to see Mr. Shutong and said that he was leaving for Suzhou that evening. If there was an opportunity in Shanghai, he would return immediately. As long as he could make a living, he wouldn't care about anything.

"Why be so attached to Shanghai?" I asked.

"Actually, a change of environment is also good, but it seems like I can't leave Shanghai."

"I really want to go to Suzhou."

"It's a pity that we can't exchange jobs!"

Because he still had some trivial matters to finish before leaving, he asked us to visit Suzhou during the spring break this year. "It's paradise over there!" he said with a smile before leaving.

This smile ended his life. The life of paradise is ultimately not something that ordinary people like us can enjoy. The reason why he couldn't leave Shanghai was probably because of this.

I received two letters from him this spring. I really wanted to take a short trip to clear my head, but literary figures have to eat every day when they are alive, and they don't have the good fortune to travel during the spring break. Besides, Suzhou is paradise! Thus, we missed our last chance to meet. However, in hindsight, it is also good, the so-called "beauty of imperfection" in poetry. Although separation and death are the most painful situations in life, there is no feast in the world that does not end. Leaving this sinful world to go to the Land of Ultimate Bliss is a path that many people are running towards.

Tianfang is dead. His colleagues at the dinner party will surely lament that heaven did not grant him more years, but what does it matter to the deceased? Therefore, I titled my lament for Han Juntianfang to lament why he had to come to this world as a passerby. Since he is dead, and is a person who has not benefited the country or the family, even if he is said to be a promising young man!

On the Rice Fields

— Qian

The people of Xu Village have already despaired! There are many rice seedlings that have not been planted, and those that have been planted are wilting under the scorching sun, showing signs of death. Even if a heavy rain of two or three feet deep fell immediately, it probably wouldn't be able to revive the short, yellow early rice that is lying weakly in the iron-hard, cracked paddy fields. But looking at the sky, it is still a bow-shaped sheet of green iron, thickly covering people's hopes. They have long known that they are in despair, but they are still desperately running to the shallow river two or three miles away to grab water, as if they would not rest in peace if they did not do this work of blood and sweat!

Changfu's mother happened to be in labor, writhing in pain on the edge of the bed. Sweat soaked through her cloth clothes. Changfu watched his mother in so much pain, but he could do nothing but cry with her. He had to bite the bullet and run out of the dilapidated house, thinking of calling his father back from the field.

Xu Da was carrying two buckets of muddy water that he had snatched with all his might. He was running quickly with his bare back, and the beads of sweat squeezed out of his back slipped down, reflecting on the ground along his footprints, but they were swallowed by the sun in an instant.

"Dad! Mom..."

"Good, Changfu! You came at the right time, quickly put those two buckets on your shoulders and go with me to the stinky river in the west to grab water!"

"Dad! No, Mom is..."

"Don't be nagging! You've been hiding at home and playing enough. Hurry up and come with me. The Chebian Pond and the River Temple are already completely dry. There's still some water at the stinky river, but if we're late, it will be snatched by others!"

Xu Da said, and started walking with the load on his shoulders. Changfu didn't dare to say anything more and followed, shedding tears.

It was already evening, but the sun was still fiercely chasing and burning them, scorching Changfu's skin. His eyes were blurry and confused, and his body was about to faint, but he didn't dare to sit down and rest for even a minute. Carrying this load on his shoulders for half the day, blisters had almost formed, and his leg bones were weak and trembling, but he still followed Xu Da desperately.

"Little devil, hurry up and carry before the night is completely dark! Don't you see how dry the fields are? If we have another famine this year, do you think we'll have rice to eat?" Xu Da scolded Changfu and urged him to hurry up.

The gentle breeze of the evening brushed Changfu's face, and his mind seemed to clear up a bit. He suddenly remembered the scene of his mother writhing in pain on the bed, and he knew that his mother hadn't eaten anything for the past two days... It was as if he could hear his mother's moaning cries: "Changfu! ... Changfu! Chang..."

"Dad!" he said with a burst of courage, "Will it be okay if I carry this load?"

Xu Da didn't answer, as if he hadn't heard, and continued running towards the river with the load on his shoulders. So Changfu perked up his spirits and asked again:

"Dad, can I go back?"

Xu Da immediately turned around, "What!"

"Mom is writhing in pain at home, calling me!"

"Who heard that, you idiot! If the fields die, not even your mother will be spared. We will all die!" Although Changfu didn't dare to disobey and run away, his heart had already run past the rice fields, stumbled into the house, and was crying and comforting his mother. His mind was filled with images of his mother writhing in pain, and he could only hear his mother's cries: "Changfu! ... Changfu, Chang..."

A Failed Subject

— Yi An

Home

— Fei Er

Dark home! Your son, who has wandered overseas for five years, has returned!

Home? You have a rotten soul, a moldy hall, a melancholy heart, and annoying noises... Home! Home!

Mother laughed until tears flowed. She stammered, "You're here today? You're here today?" She couldn't say anything else. How could I not return for your sake, you lovely face?

Grandmother had the face of a child with the hair of a crane, and was as healthy as ever. She gazed at her grandson approaching and said, "Is that Cheng'er? Is that Cheng'er? Oh, you've grown taller? Grown taller? Seeing you makes me so happy, so happy!"

Father sat smiling in a back chair in the corner of the hall. You kind old man!

The children found two crocodiles in my travel basket. They were frightened and ran away at first, then they watched, and finally they picked them up and played with them.

Thus, escaping from the embrace of the lovely, warm equatorial country, I had fallen back into this ancient family.

But dark home! This place has a broken soul, a moldy hall, a melancholy heart, and annoying noises...

Again unable to endure the encirclement of this rotten atmosphere, and wanting to escape the oppression that this ancient, dilapidated old house placed upon the wandering son, I then slipped out of that tall and solemn doorway.

Oh, the old feudal family!

But as the time passed on the belly of the monster, the fire wheel carrying me, I thought of this dark old house again. The moment of parting: mother's tears flowed, grandmother was dazed, father's face sank into a bitter smile, and the adorable siblings clung to my clothes, crying and refusing to let go.

Thinking of the gloomy old house made my head ache; but thinking of the people who loved me far away from that place, how could my heart not pound with pain?

Oh, dark old house that I had stayed in for ten days like a hotel after five years of separation, goodbye! Grandmother, parents, and adorable siblings, please forgive your wandering son and brother who is flowing with the times!

Oh, when will there be a new home to support you?

Soviet Youth's Flying Game (Part 2)

— (Moscow Dispatch) (Yin Yuan)

(3) A beautiful picture

During the Aviation Festival last August, there was such a beautiful sight in the location of the school. That is, sixty-two paratroopers jumped bravely into the air at the same time from a squadron of airplanes. Sixty-two sunflowers of various colors bloomed instantly in the blue sky and white sun. These sixty-two paratroopers all belonged to the school. Due to their brave example, they attracted many new members. Now, in one place in Moscow, there are dozens of paratrooper research groups, most of them in factories. Schools and groups have also been established in various provinces, in Ukraine, and in major cities such as Rostov and Leningrad.

The effect of paratrooping on the human body structure has not yet been studied in detail, but the school plans to begin studying this issue this year. What is particularly worth pointing out here is that people over the age of forty can also learn this game with great success.

This game is definitely not limited to men, because many women have already had multiple successful falls and have become instructors. Some men have refused to jump multiple times due to fear, but this has never happened among women, which is indeed a noteworthy thing. If a woman has decided to jump, she will resolutely carry out her resolution.

In addition to the usual style of paratrooping, the above-mentioned school also teaches people to descend slowly. This type of descent starts from a height of several thousand meters and requires a lot of strength and courage to achieve. Here, the paratroopers will jump from a long distance at a high altitude and wait until they are only a few hundred meters from the ground before releasing the parachute. The effect obtained from this type of jump that has already been tested can prove that the human body structure can maintain strong effort.

In short, parachuting has practical and scientific value, and the Soviet Union is commonly developing this game.

On the River

— Ren Ying

On the river, the ocean wind is blowing quite fiercely. Almost, the gentleman's white cork hat was blown away.

Fei sat on the stern of the boat, and the waves splashed up like raindrops. It was pitch black all around, and only the sound of the rushing river could be heard. The light of the lighthouse flashed on and off every second. Looking back at Shanghai, it was shrouded in a red cloud, hazy.

The boat was interwoven with glaring lights, and the radio broadcast charming melodies. Several blue-eyed foreigners hummed "La la! La la la" all the way to Wusong.

On the white canvas chairs, everyone had a smile on their lips. The fragrance of 4711 irritated the nose and was blown away by a gust of sea wind, then dissipated in another gust. The women's hair was blown into a mess by the gusts of sea wind. Western ladies pressed their delicate hat brims against their permed hair.

Frivolous laughter enveloped the entire deck. On the river, every young couple was wasting their youth.

A bald gentleman was lying sound asleep on a rattan chair. His snores were scattered in the melody of the ocean wind. Two companions of the opposite sex teased his sleeping posture and smiled, while they leisurely smoked cigarettes, gazing at the star-filled sky.

Sipping beer, the cool river breeze caressed their faces. How tasteful it was, watching the moving postures of everyone. The women of June possessed a multifaceted temptation, seducing the wavering youth under the city's erotic culture. Bright red lychees and silver apricots were thrown into the heart of the river, the faint sound of the waves floating away with the white foam at the stern of the boat.

Qingning Temple and Donggou gradually fell behind; the street lights along the river in Gaoqiao could be seen. The wind suffocated everyone, blowing the shawls on the women's shoulders, like the wings of the Statue of Liberty waving.

Pairs of couples slipped onto the dock. The shadows of the dimly lit buses were moving. The road towards the Seaside Hotel.

The engine of the yellow ferry started again, and there were fewer people on the deck. Wearily leaning back in the chair, touring the night Huangpu River, I scattered back into the urban crowd with a cool heart.

Fiction

Simpleton (3)

— Lin Bin

"Simpleton, fetch me water! I'll give you fragrant rice to eat."

"Fetch me some water too, simpleton. I have old wine as potent as tiger's blood!"

"Do you want to eat honey-sweet white rice candy? If you do, fetch me water!"

All sorts of honey-sweet, crisp voices floated from all directions into the simpleton's ears, pricking his nerves like needle tips, causing an odd excitement to rise throughout his body. He kept glancing this way and that, humming, "So pretty, so pretty!" Finally, he gave them all a common answer:

"Carry, carry!"

And so, amidst admiring murmurs and enthusiastic encouragement, one load, two loads, three loads... "Rest a while, simpleton! Eat something before carrying more!"

The simpleton cheerfully obeyed.

Then another load, two loads, three loads...

Carrying water wasn't the most strenuous task for a strong farmer, but a pair of large cypress buckets, famous throughout the village (seven or eight times out of ten, they would borrow these buckets when asking the simpleton to carry water), combined with the slippery, rain-soaked path where one could easily fall, and the round trip distance of a full "li" (about half a kilometer), were not easy for the simpleton, whose flesh was gradually separating from his large bones under the torment of an inhuman existence. After carrying ten loads of brimming well water in a row, he panted like an old ox overworked on a hot day, his legs trembling, unable to stand steady. As usual, he first sat for a moment on the edge of the steps, and then leaned back, silently lying on his back on the cool, shady mud.

"Oh, are you tired, simpleton? Rest a while longer! Rest and then fetch me a few loads too. I'll be your matchmaker!"

The simpleton weakly shook his head, indicating that he couldn't carry any more.

"Rest a while longer. If you can't carry full loads, carry half loads, I'll be your matchmaker!"

And so, in less than half an hour, the carrying pole with the heavy cypress buckets was once again pressing down on his shoulders.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special Issue

Banning Male-Female Co-starring Films Amidst the Retro Movement (Part 1)

— Dan Feng

The era has progressed to 1934, truly a strange year in China. This is not only because the heat is reaching levels unseen in sixty years, but more importantly, the insane retro movement is making us feel most surprised and most afraid.

The so-called retro movement naturally aims to return China to a very ancient era, or in other words, to drive backwards, as everyone says. But driving backwards is a very difficult task after all, because there is always the danger of pushing the passengers in the carriages into deep pits or large rivers. If this were to happen, the poor passengers would naturally die unjustly, but the commanders in the engine room could ignore this. However, even so, the retro movement is indeed being vigorously promoted by the literati and gentlemen, who are shouting themselves hoarse. Regarding their achievements, we can cite many, from the revival of classical Chinese to the prohibition of men and women walking together… they are almost magnificently abundant. And now, according to newspaper reports, in Guangdong, the place that opened up to the outside world earliest and is the cradle of revolution, it has already progressed (?) to banning male-female co-starring films.

Here, regarding that grand and righteous ban, it seems necessary to respectfully transcribe and reprint it. "(1) Men and women are prohibited from riding in the same vehicle, (2) Men and women are prohibited from eating together (regardless of government offices, families, teahouses, or restaurants, men and women are uniformly prohibited from eating together. Women must wait until the men have finished eating before they can eat.), (3) Men and women are prohibited from living together (hotels are uniformly prohibited from allowing men and women to live in the same room.), (4) Military personnel and civilians are prohibited from walking together, (5) Movie theaters are prohibited from showing films with male and female co-stars. As for General Chen Bonan's advocacy of venerating the classics and restoring antiquity, and Naval Commander Zhang Zhiying's proposal to prohibit men and women from swimming together and to differentiate between men and women with loose hair, all cases have been fully passed and implemented by the association." In front of the ban, there are still the following sentences that must be copied verbatim: "Since the New Life Movement, in addition to the so-called ban on men and women walking together, there are also so-called orders prohibiting men and women from living and eating together, and the Guangdong Political Research Association has further passed the following gender boundaries." Moreover, the reporter was even bolder later, and added an editor's note saying: "However, the young men and women of the general era all believe it is extremely boring and strongly oppose it."

The above articles, from one to four, can be said to be outside the scope of this article, only the fifth article concerning the instructions to the movie theaters, then we really only have to call for grievance and injustice. Needless to say, film, in this situation, can only die out completely. The reason is very simple, because film is an art that reflects the reality of society, and society has men and women, it was so in the past, it is so now, and it will be so in the future, then naturally there must be men and women in films as well. (To be continued)

Film Review

Review of "Looking for Trouble"

— Dan Feng

Looking for Trouble, Nanjing

Not long ago, Cathay screened a Warner Bros. production called "The Voice of the City," which was themed around telephones, writing about a brave and resourceful telephone worker who, because of his diligent service, and especially his efforts to help an old boss recover lost funds, ended up getting some rewards and marrying a female telephone operator. Now, this "Looking for Trouble" produced by 20th Century Fox is also themed around telephones, also writing about a telephone worker who, after working hard and accomplishing great things, happily marries an operator.

The content of the films being so similar is by no means an accidental fact. On the contrary, it precisely illustrates how filmmakers are vying for audiences. However, they do not compete in terms of content, but merely in hunting for the same themes. Thus, one company begins filming a movie with the theme of playing ball, and soon everyone rushes to imitate it, and movies about playing ball become popular for a while. In addition, beast films or detective films have all filled the market for a time, and in the future, perhaps there will be several more films based on telephones appearing? This is very possible.

But we believe that if we compare Fay Enright's "Voice of the City" with this William Wellman's "Looking for Trouble," then we will think that the latter is inferior to the former. In this film, we certainly cannot say that there are no achievements at all, at least a few witty remarks are very amusing. But comparatively speaking, relying solely on a few witty remarks cannot cover up the excessive dull scenes in the play, and among them, the three more tense parts, (1) Uncle Duke digging a tunnel to steal funds until Joe and Kaiser are captured, (2) Joe pressing the fire alarm to send out the fire truck fleet, (3) The sudden earthquake: none of them can excellently grab the audience's emotions. Especially the latter two, the director uses them as climaxes, but because the transition from climax to low point is too fast, people feel that the climax did not fully exert its due power, resulting in us feeling that the two climaxes were superfluous. Regarding this point, it is naturally the relationship of editing, the director's montage is indeed not very brilliant. Compared with "Voice of the City," the consistent maintenance of humor from beginning to end is enough to show the weakness of this film.

There is a kind of film that is a victory of formalism, making people unable to directly feel the vulgarity and unpleasantness of the story, while there is a kind that cannot hide the emptiness or mediocrity of the content. "Looking for Trouble" should belong to the latter type.

We believe that good actors can never unfold their skills in mediocre directing techniques. Spencer Tracy acted very well in Frank Borzage's "Man's Castle," but here he is only competent. Jack Oakie is okay, but Constance Cummings is again mediocre.

Regarding William Wellman, we have seen many of his works, and most of them are very mature, but this film, we dare not praise.

Gloria Swanson, a Female Star Who Has Been Divorced Four Times, Is About to Divorce Again

— He Qin

Divorce is not a strange thing in Hollywood, but it is indeed rare for a male or female star to be divorced three or four times in a row. Not long ago, we heard that John Gilbert had been divorced four times. But recently, Hollywood discovered that Gloria Swanson, a female star famous for her coquettishness, is also a person who has been divorced three times. Recently, it is said that because her husband does not want her to return to the screen, she is preparing to file for divorce again. Like this taking marriage as child's play, Gilbert and she are truly a pair.

Her first husband was Wallace Beery, who is now very famous on the screen. The second husband was the deceased Herbert Somborn; the boss of the "Brown Derby" restaurant in Hollywood; the third was the French Marquis Henri de la Falaise; now Constance Bennett's husband. Finally, she married her current, still unseparated, fourth husband, named Michael Farmer. He is the youngest and most handsome of her four husbands, and is much younger than she is herself.

They first met in Europe. The two fell in love at first sight and made a pact of lifelong commitment, and she retired from the film industry. For two years, she followed her young husband back and forth between Europe and America, and they got along very well. Who knew that she recently wanted to return to the stage and reappear on the screen, but her husband was very opposed to it, so the two inevitably started to argue. A few weeks ago, Michael left Hollywood alone in a fit of pique, while Swanson still lived there, so the matter of their divorce is even more loudly discussed in Hollywood. According to Swanson herself, their divorce is probably unavoidable!

The Posthumous Honor of Marie Dressler

— Luo Yu

When Marie Dressler was crowned Queen of Hollywood at the age of sixty, it was truly a sensation in the world's film industry. All past queens have had beautiful faces and youthful ages, but in the year that Marie Dressler became queen, she was already white-haired. She once competed with her ugly husband Wallace Beery to see who was uglier, but she occupied the queen's throne under the gaze of Hollywood stars, it was truly unprecedented in Hollywood history. At that time, the praise and public opinion were also rare in Hollywood.

Now, this old star has passed away, and after the news of her death spread from Hollywood, the film industry was very saddened. Many Hollywood stars sent telegrams of condolences, and the film industries of various European countries also sent telegrams to the United States to mourn. Since the founding of the United States, only Lincoln's death had such a lively atmosphere. Apart from that, no one has been able to compare.

Marie was born on November 9, 1871. When she celebrated her sixtieth birthday, the wife of former US President Hoover celebrated her birthday in Washington. Marie was the first to have such glory in the history of the film industry. When Marie was critically ill at the Saint Bernerd's Hospital, President Roosevelt's wife also visited in person to offer condolences. Overseas telegrams were also like snowflakes. It can be seen that Marie was respected. After her death, many of Hollywood's top stars personally went to offer condolences. It is said that after Valentino's death, there were thousands of mourners. Now Marie Dressler's funeral should be no less than that of those years.

One thing that can be considered a pity after Marie's death is that she had no relatives behind her. There was only a distant cousin in her home, otherwise there were none.

Although Marie worked a lot throughout her life and earned a lot of money, she did not have much property before her death. She was very frugal in her daily life, and did not waste all the money she had. But because she has always liked good deeds and constantly helped many poor people, all her property was used up. The poor people in the United States who had received her help could not help but cry for her this time she died.

Marie had made a will two weeks before her death. She instructed that all the money she had earned throughout her life should be used to help the poor, disabled, and elderly. She only asked to be buried immediately after her death, and had no other concerns. In addition, she also said that she had done many plays in the film industry, and now it was the closing of a real drama.

Unfulfilled Private Wish

— Lun

A long time ago, there was a beautiful girl who wholeheartedly wanted to become a nun. She often fantasized about becoming a nun and retreating to a convent symbolizing peace and quiet. Who was she? It was Helen Hayes.

However, this lovely girl did not realize her early private wish, at least she did not have the opportunity to play this role during her stage life, but in the film "White Sister," she played the role of a nun, and performed very well. To this day, this is still her most proud masterpiece.

Movie Novel

Good Son, Good Wife (Born to be Kissed) (12)

— Xin Zhi

The prison door on Jefferson Street opened, and Tom strode in. Edie raised her haggard face, her eyes already swollen from crying, she saw Tom, and couldn't help but cheer. She hugged him and shouted, "I knew you would come, hold me tight!" Tom embraced her for a while, then let her go, looked at her face and asked, "Who exactly was that person, that you were found with?" Edie cried out in grievance, "I don't even know him! It was all a set-up by them! You have to believe me! If you don't believe me, I don't want to live anymore!" Tom hesitated for a moment, then said, "I do believe you, but who do you think set you up to frame you?" Hearing this, Edie felt warmth in her eyes, and her lips trembled. She shouted hatefully, "I know! It's none other than your father! I know it clearly, as if I heard him design and arrange it with my own ears! They accused me of stealing Kershaw's emerald... only your father knew about that, it was Kershaw who gave it to me face to face!" At this time, Pan Qi was standing outside the iron cage. He heard Edie's words, and pretended to be very kind, saying to Tom, "Son, I heard what Edie said. But her nerves are about to break down. She has suffered a lot." Edie stared at Pan Qi with both eyes and shouted, "You know! This is all your doing!" Tom persuaded, "Edie, don't be like this, Father came specially to bail you out!" Edie said, "Bail me out? I know! He's here to bail me out of your life!" She cried. Pan Qi was next to her, still pretending to be benevolent and righteous, saying, "You shouldn't have shown those two gems to people." Edie said, "Kershaw gave them to me... you know it clearly!" Pan Qi said, "Edie, if you want to say that, I can't do anything about it. But I regret keeping them for you. Being involved in this kind of case is not a good thing after all." Hearing this, Edie cursed at him, "You old hypocrite!" Tom asked doubtfully, "Why did you take those things to keep with my father?" Hearing this, Edie knew that Pan Qi had already buried suspicion and disbelief in his son's heart, and shouted like crazy, "Why? It's because I was afraid that the police wouldn't believe me, so I asked him for help!" Tom said, "Didn't Father also give you money to go to another place?" Edie said, "Is that what he told you? That money was lent to me by him... but he didn't say anything about going to another place. I haven't committed any crime, why should I run away?" Tom said: "But you did go out..." Pan Qi said again, "What are you to Kershaw, tell Tom." Edie said, "I'm nothing to him. He is also nothing to me. That night, it was the first time I met him. This is all the truth, Tom." She looked at Tom with tear-filled eyes, pleadingly. Tom said, "Didn't you say that he was willing to marry you... and you were already engaged?" Edie said, "I... he did ask me to marry him, but maybe he was deliberately fooling me..." Pan Qi interjected, "What do you mean? Wasn't he about to commit suicide?" Edie was even more aware of Pan Qi's cunning by his interruption, and couldn't help but curse loudly again, "You old thing who tells lies and plots to harm people!" She was extremely disappointed, knowing that she could not fight against the old diplomat who was deep in thought. Pan Qi then turned to his son and said, "Son, she has almost answered all the questions. Tom looked at his father inexplicably, and then looked at Edie. (To be continued)
